Generating data fetching code...

import pandas as pd
import requests
import os

def download_data():
    # Set the base URL, email, and API key
    base_url = "https://aqs.epa.gov/data/api/annualData/byState"
    email = "teakinboyewa@gmail.com"
    api_key = "tawnyswift57"

    # Parameters for the API request
    params = {
        "email": email,
        "key": api_key,
        "param": "88101",  # PM2.5 FRM/FEM
        "bdate": "20190101",
        "edate": "20191231",
        "state": "06"  # California
    }

    # Make the request to the EPA AQS API
    response = requests.get(base_url, params=params)
    response_json = response.json()

    # Check if the request was successful
    if response_json['Header'][0]['status'] == 'Success':
        # Extract data from the response
        data = response_json['Data']

        # Convert the data into a pandas DataFrame
        df = pd.DataFrame(data)

        # Filter for quality-assured observations
        df = df[df['validity_indicator'] == 'Y']

        # Define the output directory and ensure it exists
        output_dir = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput"
        os.makedirs(output_dir, exist_ok=True)

        # Save the DataFrame to a CSV in the specified directory
        output_file = os.path.join(output_dir, "PM2.5_Annual_California_2019.csv")
        df.to_csv(output_file, index=False)
    else:
        # If the request was not successful, print the message
        print("Failed to retrieve data: ", response_json['Header'][0]['msg'])

# Call the function to execute the data download
download_data()

Generating data fetching code...

import requests
import csv
import json

def download_data():
    # Define the endpoint, year, and API key
    base_url = "https://api.census.gov/data/2019/acs/acs5"
    api_key = "918876e93cf30566c02b367fcad29644d861817e"
    dataset_year = "2019"
    dataset_source = f"ACS {dataset_year}"

    # Variables needed to fetch
    variables = [
        # B19083_001E:Gini Index of Income Inequality
        "B19083_001E"
    ]

    # Fetch the variable labels for descriptions
    response = requests.get(f"{base_url}/variables.json")
    variables_metadata = response.json()

    # Helper function to get variable labels without 'Estimate!!'
    def get_variable_label(var_name):
        label = variables_metadata['variables'][var_name]['label']
        return label.replace("Estimate!!", "").strip()

    # Construct the URL for fetching Gini coefficient data for California counties
    get_vars = ",".join(variables)
    url = f"{base_url}?get={get_vars}&for=county:*&in=state:06&key={api_key}" # '06' is the FIPS code for California

    # Download data from Census API
    response = requests.get(url)
    response.raise_for_status()
    data = response.json()

    # Prepare the path to save the CSV file
    output_directory = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput"
    csv_path = f"{output_directory}/California_Counties_Gini_2019.csv"

    # Create headers with variable labels
    header = [f"{var}:{get_variable_label(var)}" for var in variables] + ["state_fips", "county_fips", "year", "source"]
    rows = data[1:]  # Skip the header row provided by API
    for row in rows:
        row.extend([dataset_year, dataset_source])

    # Write to CSV file
    with open(csv_path, mode='w', newline='') as file:
        writer = csv.writer(file)
        writer.writerow(header)
        writer.writerows(rows)

# Execute the function
download_data()

This code will retrieve the Gini Index data for California counties in 2019 from the U.S. Census Bureau API and store it in the specified output directory. The described methodologies ensure proper labeling and formatting according to the technical requirements.

Generating data fetching code...

import requests
import pandas as pd

def download_data():
    # Step 1: Define URLs
    base_url = "https://gisportal.ers.usda.gov/server/rest/services/Rural_Atlas_Data/County_Classifications/MapServer"
    layer_id = 0
    layer_metadata_url = f"{base_url}/{layer_id}?f=json"
    data_query_url = f"{base_url}/{layer_id}/query"

    # Step 2: Get layer metadata to identify field names and other capabilities
    metadata_response = requests.get(layer_metadata_url)
    metadata = metadata_response.json()

    # List recognized fields from metadata
    assert 'fields' in metadata, "Metadata does not include fields"
    field_names = [field['name'] for field in metadata['fields']]

    # Step 3: Determine the total count of records
    count_query_params = {
        'where': '1=1',
        'returnCountOnly': 'true',
        'f': 'json'
    }
    count_response = requests.get(data_query_url, params=count_query_params)
    total_records = count_response.json().get('count', 0)

    # Step 4: Fetch data in pages if necessary
    results = []
    result_offset = 0
    max_records_per_query = 1000

    while result_offset < total_records:
        record_query_params = {
            'where': '1=1',
            'outFields': '*',
            'f': 'json',
            'returnGeometry': 'false',
            'outSR': '4326',
            'resultOffset': result_offset,
            'resultRecordCount': max_records_per_query
        }
        record_response = requests.get(data_query_url, params=record_query_params)
        data = record_response.json()
        features = data.get("features", [])

        # Extract attributes from each feature
        for feature in features:
            results.append(feature["attributes"])

        # Check if we should continue pagination
        if not data.get("exceededTransferLimit", False):
            break

        result_offset += max_records_per_query

    # Step 5: Convert gathered data into a DataFrame
    df = pd.DataFrame(results)

    # Step 6: Filter data for California counties only (FIPSTXT starts with '06')
    df = df[df['FIPSTXT'].str.startswith('06')]

    # Step 7: Save the dataframe as a CSV
    output_path = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput/California_UrbanRural_Classification_2019.csv"
    df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)

download_data()

This script follows the detailed guidelines for downloading and processing geospatial data, specifically focusing on urban-rural classifications for California counties from a USDA ERS data service. It first gathers metadata to understand the fields and capabilities of the service, then queries the data in pages, filters for California counties, and saves the result to a CSV file in the specified directory.

Generating data fetching code...

import geopandas as gpd

def download_data():
    # URL construction for California county boundaries for the year 2019
    # Following the technical handbook, 'extend' should be 'us' for downloading county boundaries
    # For year 2019, the link becomes: https://www2.census.gov/geo/tiger/GENZ2019/shp/cb_2019_us_county_500k.zip
    url = "https://www2.census.gov/geo/tiger/GENZ2019/shp/cb_2019_us_county_500k.zip"

    # Loading the shapefile from the URL directly using geopandas
    counties = gpd.read_file(url)

    # Filtering the data to retain only California counties 
    # California's FIPS state code is '06'
    california_counties = counties[counties['STATEFP'] == '06']

    # Define the output directory and file path
    output_path = '/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput/california_counties_2019.gpkg'

    # Save the data to a GeoPackage
    california_counties.to_file(output_path, driver='GPKG')

# Execute the function to download and save the data
download_data()

import os
import pandas as pd

# Paths
INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput/PM2.5_Annual_California_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_2019_annual_records.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

# Load
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH, dtype=str)

# Filter (columns confirmed by get_columns)
mask = (df["year"].astype(str).str.strip() == "2019") & (
    df["pollutant_standard"].astype(str).str.strip() == "PM25 Annual 2006"
)

out_df = df.loc[mask, ["state_code", "county_code", "site_number", "arithmetic_mean"]].copy()

# Save
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)
out_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

# Record artifact (intermediate dataset)
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_PATH,
    caption="Filtered PM2.5 annual 2019 records for California under the 'PM25 Annual 2006' standard, retaining site identifiers and arithmetic mean.",
    viz_hint={"type": "table"},
    role="intermediate",
)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=create FIPS GEOID by concatenating zero-padded state and county codes in pandas, section=)

--- Reading skill doc: 'create FIPS GEOID by concatenating zero-padded state and county codes in pandas' ---

Data Merging (Join, Merge, Spatial Join)

Description

Combine two tables by a shared key (pd.merge) or by geometry (gpd.sjoin).
The correctness of every downstream step depends on the match rate — a
silent join that produces NaN for 50% of rows will poison later modeling.

When to use

  • Linking attribute data (CSV) to polygons (GeoPackage/SHP) on FIPS/GEOID.
  • Combining variables from two CSV sources on a shared key.
  • Enriching points/polygons via spatial containment.

When NOT to use

  • Reshape only (pivot/melt) — not a merge.
  • Concatenating rows of identical schema — use pd.concat.

Critical constraints

  1. Always cast join keys to string and zfill to a consistent width
    before merging. Int-vs-string and missing-leading-zero mismatches silently
    drop every match.
  2. State FIPS: zfill(2) (e.g. "06").
  3. County FIPS: zfill(3) (e.g. "001").
  4. County GEOID (state+county): zfill(5) (e.g. "06001").
  5. Tract GEOID: zfill(11).
  6. Strip whitespace on both keys: .astype(str).str.strip().
  7. Replace Census sentinels with NaN on any ACS/Decennial column:
    df.replace(-666666666, np.nan, inplace=True). Values like -999999999,
    -888888888, -666666666 are Census "suppressed / not available" codes
    — not real numbers.
  8. Audit and print match rate after every merge. A match rate below 90%
    is a red flag — either keys are mis-formatted or the right-side dataset
    doesn't cover all left-side units (report both hypotheses).
  9. Left join keeps every left row — NaN on the right side does NOT raise
    an error. You must inspect the output for NaN, not just row count.
  10. For spatial joins, both GeoDataFrames must be in the same projected
    CRS.     Reproject before sjoin.

Paths

  • INPUT_PATH_LEFT, INPUT_PATH_RIGHT — from the step's Input Node Paths.
  • OUTPUT_NODE_PATH — merged primary output.
  • OUTPUT_DIR — directory for join-audit log.

Never hardcode "data.csv", "dataset_a.csv", etc.

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# ---- 1. Load ------------------------------------------------------------
left  = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)   # polygons (or a GeoDataFrame)
right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")
right = right.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------
merged = left.merge(right, left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- 5. AUDIT the merge -------------------------------------------------
right_added = [c for c in right.columns if c != RIGHT_KEY and c in merged.columns]
audit_col   = right_added[0] if right_added else None

if audit_col is not None:
    matched      = int(merged[audit_col].notna().sum())
    total        = len(merged)
    match_rate   = matched / total if total else 0.0
    unmatched_n  = total - matched

    audit_lines = [
        f"[JOIN AUDIT] merged {total} left rows",
        f"  matched on '{audit_col}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
        f"  unmatched (NaN in right side): {unmatched_n}",
    ]
    if match_rate < 0.9:
        audit_lines.append(f"  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect keys:")
        audit_lines.append(f"    left  {LEFT_KEY} sample: {left[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        audit_lines.append(f"    right {RIGHT_KEY} sample: {right[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")
    audit = "\n".join(audit_lines)
    print(audit)
    os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    with open(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit.txt"), "w") as f:
        f.write(audit + "\n")

# ---- 6. Save primary output --------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
if isinstance(merged, gpd.GeoDataFrame):
    merged.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")
else:
    merged.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Spatial join variant (points in polygons)

import geopandas as gpd

points   = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)
polygons = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)

# Reproject to same CRS (use polygons' CRS by convention)
if points.crs != polygons.crs:
    points = points.to_crs(polygons.crs)

joined = gpd.sjoin(points, polygons, how="left", predicate="within")

# Audit — how many points landed in a polygon?
unmatched = joined["index_right"].isna().sum()
print(f"[SJOIN AUDIT] {len(joined)-unmatched}/{len(joined)} points matched a polygon "
      f"({unmatched} outside all polygons)")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Int vs string FIPS silently produces 0 matches Cast both sides to str.strip().str.zfill(W) with the right width.
Leading zeros stripped by pd.read_csv Either dtype={'GEOID': str} at read time, or zfill after load.
ACS sentinel -666666666 treated as a real value df.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan).
"58 records created" looks fine but half are NaN Always print match rate, not just row count.
sjoin returns 0 rows Reproject to a common CRS first; verify with points.within(polygons.unary_union).sum().
how="inner" after a previously-failed join Use how="left" for auditing; switch to inner only after you've verified the match rate.
Duplicated keys on the right side explode left row count right.drop_duplicates(subset=[RIGHT_KEY]) before merge if right is supposed to be unique.
Tract vs county GEOID width mismatch Decide which level the join is at; enforce the matching width on both sides.

--- End skill doc ---

import os
import pandas as pd

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_2019_annual_records.csv"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_2019_with_geoid.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH)

# ---- Load ----------------------------------------------------------------
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH)

# ---- Create county GEOID (state_code zfill(2) + county_code zfill(3)) ----
required_cols = ["state_code", "county_code"]
missing = [c for c in required_cols if c not in df.columns]
if missing:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing required columns: {missing}. Available columns: {df.columns.tolist()}")

state = df["state_code"].astype(str).str.strip()
county = df["county_code"].astype(str).str.strip()

# Treat common "missing" string tokens as NA after string conversion
na_tokens = {"", "nan", "none", "null", "<na>"}
state_is_na = state.str.lower().isin(na_tokens)
county_is_na = county.str.lower().isin(na_tokens)

df["GEOID"] = pd.NA
mask = (~state_is_na) & (~county_is_na)
df.loc[mask, "GEOID"] = state.loc[mask].str.zfill(2) + county.loc[mask].str.zfill(3)

# ---- Save ----------------------------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)
df.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_2019_with_geoid.csv"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_county_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

# ---- Load ----------------------------------------------------------------
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH, dtype=str)

# ---- Clean/normalize needed fields ---------------------------------------
# GEOID: strip; zfill to modal width to preserve leading zeros (county GEOID usually width=5)
df["GEOID"] = df["GEOID"].astype(str).str.strip()
geoid_len = df["GEOID"].dropna().str.len()
if not geoid_len.empty:
    key_width = int(geoid_len.mode().iloc[0])
    df["GEOID"] = df["GEOID"].str.zfill(key_width)

# arithmetic_mean: numeric for mean aggregation
df["arithmetic_mean"] = pd.to_numeric(df["arithmetic_mean"], errors="coerce")

# site_number: keep as string; count non-null per GEOID
df["site_number"] = df["site_number"].astype(str).replace({"nan": np.nan}).str.strip()

# Drop rows without GEOID (cannot aggregate)
df = df.dropna(subset=["GEOID"])

# ---- Aggregate ------------------------------------------------------------
out = (
    df.groupby("GEOID", as_index=False)
    .agg(
        pm25_mean_2019=("arithmetic_mean", "mean"),
        pm25_site_count_2019=("site_number", "count"),
    )
)

# ---- Save ----------------------------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)
out.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

--- Reading skill doc: 'left join CSV to GeoPackage on GEOID using geopandas merge' ---

Data Merging (Join, Merge, Spatial Join)

Description

Combine two tables by a shared key (pd.merge) or by geometry (gpd.sjoin).
The correctness of every downstream step depends on the match rate — a
silent join that produces NaN for 50% of rows will poison later modeling.

When to use

  • Linking attribute data (CSV) to polygons (GeoPackage/SHP) on FIPS/GEOID.
  • Combining variables from two CSV sources on a shared key.
  • Enriching points/polygons via spatial containment.

When NOT to use

  • Reshape only (pivot/melt) — not a merge.
  • Concatenating rows of identical schema — use pd.concat.

Critical constraints

  1. Always cast join keys to string and zfill to a consistent width
    before merging. Int-vs-string and missing-leading-zero mismatches silently
    drop every match.
  2. State FIPS: zfill(2) (e.g. "06").
  3. County FIPS: zfill(3) (e.g. "001").
  4. County GEOID (state+county): zfill(5) (e.g. "06001").
  5. Tract GEOID: zfill(11).
  6. Strip whitespace on both keys: .astype(str).str.strip().
  7. Replace Census sentinels with NaN on any ACS/Decennial column:
    df.replace(-666666666, np.nan, inplace=True). Values like -999999999,
    -888888888, -666666666 are Census "suppressed / not available" codes
    — not real numbers.
  8. Audit and print match rate after every merge. A match rate below 90%
    is a red flag — either keys are mis-formatted or the right-side dataset
    doesn't cover all left-side units (report both hypotheses).
  9. Left join keeps every left row — NaN on the right side does NOT raise
    an error. You must inspect the output for NaN, not just row count.
  10. For spatial joins, both GeoDataFrames must be in the same projected
    CRS.     Reproject before sjoin.

Paths

  • INPUT_PATH_LEFT, INPUT_PATH_RIGHT — from the step's Input Node Paths.
  • OUTPUT_NODE_PATH — merged primary output.
  • OUTPUT_DIR — directory for join-audit log.

Never hardcode "data.csv", "dataset_a.csv", etc.

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------

        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")

    print(audit)

points   = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Int vs string FIPS silently produces 0 matches Cast both sides to str.strip().str.zfill(W) with the right width.
Leading zeros stripped by pd.read_csv Either dtype={'GEOID': str} at read time, or zfill after load.

--- End skill doc ---

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# Manuscript artifact helpers are pre-imported:
# record_figure, record_table, record_data_to_viz

INPUT_COUNTIES = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput/california_counties_2019.gpkg"
INPUT_PM25 = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_county_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_GPKG = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_GPKG), exist_ok=True)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# -----------------------
# Load
# -----------------------
counties = gpd.read_file(INPUT_COUNTIES)
pm25 = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PM25)

# -----------------------
# Validate/clean geometry
# -----------------------
counties = counties[counties.geometry.notna()]
counties = counties[counties.geometry.is_valid & ~counties.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# -----------------------
# Prepare join keys
# -----------------------
JOIN_KEY = "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5  # County GEOID is state(2)+county(3)

counties[JOIN_KEY] = counties[JOIN_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
pm25[JOIN_KEY] = pm25[JOIN_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# Keep only the required right-side columns
pm25_keep = ["GEOID", "pm25_mean_2019", "pm25_site_count_2019"]
missing_right = [c for c in pm25_keep if c not in pm25.columns]
if missing_right:
    raise KeyError(
        f"Missing required columns in pm25 CSV: {missing_right}. "
        f"Available columns: {list(pm25.columns)}"
    )
pm25 = pm25[pm25_keep].copy()

# Coerce PM2.5 fields to numeric (they arrived as object)
pm25["pm25_mean_2019"] = pd.to_numeric(pm25["pm25_mean_2019"], errors="coerce")
pm25["pm25_site_count_2019"] = pd.to_numeric(pm25["pm25_site_count_2019"], errors="coerce")

# Replace common sentinel values if present
pm25 = pm25.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# Ensure right-side key uniqueness (avoid exploding row counts)
pm25 = pm25.drop_duplicates(subset=["GEOID"]).copy()

# -----------------------
# Left join
# -----------------------
out = counties.merge(pm25, on="GEOID", how="left")

# -----------------------
# Join audit
# -----------------------
total = len(out)
matched = int(out["pm25_mean_2019"].notna().sum())
match_rate = (matched / total) if total else 0.0
unmatched = total - matched

audit_lines = [
    "[JOIN AUDIT] Left join pm25_county_2019 to california_counties_2019 on GEOID",
    f"  left rows (counties): {total}",
    f"  matched (non-null pm25_mean_2019): {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
    f"  unmatched (null pm25_mean_2019): {unmatched}",
]
if match_rate < 0.9:
    audit_lines.append("  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect GEOID formatting/coverage.")
    audit_lines.append(f"    left GEOID sample: {counties['GEOID'].head(5).tolist()}")
    audit_lines.append(f"    right GEOID sample: {pm25['GEOID'].head(5).tolist()}")
    audit_lines.append(
        f"    example unmatched left GEOIDs: {out.loc[out['pm25_mean_2019'].isna(), 'GEOID'].head(10).tolist()}"
    )

audit_text = "\n".join(audit_lines)
print(audit_text)

audit_path = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit_pm25_2019_counties.txt")
with open(audit_path, "w") as f:
    f.write(audit_text + "\n")

# -----------------------
# Save output
# -----------------------
out.to_file(OUTPUT_GPKG, driver="GPKG")

    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,

    viz_hint={"type": "choropleth", "column": "pm25_mean_2019"},
    role="intermediate",
)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=Merging datasets by key (pandas merge) or geometry (geopandas sjoin), section=)

--- Reading skill doc: 'Merging datasets by key (pandas merge) or geometry (geopandas sjoin)' ---

Data Merging (Join, Merge, Spatial Join)

Description

Combine two tables by a shared key (pd.merge) or by geometry (gpd.sjoin).
The correctness of every downstream step depends on the match rate — a
silent join that produces NaN for 50% of rows will poison later modeling.

When to use

  • Linking attribute data (CSV) to polygons (GeoPackage/SHP) on FIPS/GEOID.
  • Combining variables from two CSV sources on a shared key.
  • Enriching points/polygons via spatial containment.

When NOT to use

  • Reshape only (pivot/melt) — not a merge.
  • Concatenating rows of identical schema — use pd.concat.

Critical constraints

  1. Always cast join keys to string and zfill to a consistent width
    before merging. Int-vs-string and missing-leading-zero mismatches silently
    drop every match.
  2. State FIPS: zfill(2) (e.g. "06").
  3. County FIPS: zfill(3) (e.g. "001").
  4. County GEOID (state+county): zfill(5) (e.g. "06001").
  5. Tract GEOID: zfill(11).
  6. Strip whitespace on both keys: .astype(str).str.strip().
  7. Replace Census sentinels with NaN on any ACS/Decennial column:
    df.replace(-666666666, np.nan, inplace=True). Values like -999999999,
    -888888888, -666666666 are Census "suppressed / not available" codes
    — not real numbers.
  8. Audit and print match rate after every merge. A match rate below 90%
    is a red flag — either keys are mis-formatted or the right-side dataset
    doesn't cover all left-side units (report both hypotheses).
  9. Left join keeps every left row — NaN on the right side does NOT raise
    an error. You must inspect the output for NaN, not just row count.
  10. For spatial joins, both GeoDataFrames must be in the same projected
    CRS.     Reproject before sjoin.

Paths

  • INPUT_PATH_LEFT, INPUT_PATH_RIGHT — from the step's Input Node Paths.
  • OUTPUT_NODE_PATH — merged primary output.
  • OUTPUT_DIR — directory for join-audit log.

Never hardcode "data.csv", "dataset_a.csv", etc.

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# ---- 1. Load ------------------------------------------------------------
left  = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)   # polygons (or a GeoDataFrame)
right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")
right = right.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------
merged = left.merge(right, left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- 5. AUDIT the merge -------------------------------------------------
right_added = [c for c in right.columns if c != RIGHT_KEY and c in merged.columns]
audit_col   = right_added[0] if right_added else None

if audit_col is not None:
    matched      = int(merged[audit_col].notna().sum())
    total        = len(merged)
    match_rate   = matched / total if total else 0.0
    unmatched_n  = total - matched

    audit_lines = [
        f"[JOIN AUDIT] merged {total} left rows",
        f"  matched on '{audit_col}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
        f"  unmatched (NaN in right side): {unmatched_n}",
    ]
    if match_rate < 0.9:
        audit_lines.append(f"  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect keys:")
        audit_lines.append(f"    left  {LEFT_KEY} sample: {left[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        audit_lines.append(f"    right {RIGHT_KEY} sample: {right[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")
    audit = "\n".join(audit_lines)
    print(audit)
    os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    with open(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit.txt"), "w") as f:
        f.write(audit + "\n")

# ---- 6. Save primary output --------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
if isinstance(merged, gpd.GeoDataFrame):
    merged.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")
else:
    merged.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Spatial join variant (points in polygons)

import geopandas as gpd

points   = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)
polygons = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)

# Reproject to same CRS (use polygons' CRS by convention)
if points.crs != polygons.crs:
    points = points.to_crs(polygons.crs)

joined = gpd.sjoin(points, polygons, how="left", predicate="within")

# Audit — how many points landed in a polygon?
unmatched = joined["index_right"].isna().sum()
print(f"[SJOIN AUDIT] {len(joined)-unmatched}/{len(joined)} points matched a polygon "
      f"({unmatched} outside all polygons)")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Int vs string FIPS silently produces 0 matches Cast both sides to str.strip().str.zfill(W) with the right width.
Leading zeros stripped by pd.read_csv Either dtype={'GEOID': str} at read time, or zfill after load.
ACS sentinel -666666666 treated as a real value df.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan).
"58 records created" looks fine but half are NaN Always print match rate, not just row count.
sjoin returns 0 rows Reproject to a common CRS first; verify with points.within(polygons.unary_union).sum().
how="inner" after a previously-failed join Use how="left" for auditing; switch to inner only after you've verified the match rate.
Duplicated keys on the right side explode left row count right.drop_duplicates(subset=[RIGHT_KEY]) before merge if right is supposed to be unique.
Tract vs county GEOID width mismatch Decide which level the join is at; enforce the matching width on both sides.

--- End skill doc ---

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=queen contiguity spatial weights libpysal, section=)

# Spatial Weights

## Description

A spatial weights matrix `W` defines which observations are neighbors and how strongly they're connected. Almost every spatial statistic (Moran's I, LISA, spatial lag/error regression) takes `W` as input.

## When to use

- Before Global or Local Moran's I.
- Before spatial regression (SAR, SEM) or GWR diagnostics.
- Any time you need to express "neighbor of" relationships between geographic units.

## When NOT to use

- Non-spatial data — no geometry, no weights.
- Purely attribute-space neighborhoods (use sklearn KNN on features instead).

## Choosing the scheme

| Scheme | Use when | Class |
|---|---|---|
| Queen contiguity | Polygons (counties, tracts); neighbors share edge or vertex | `libpysal.weights.Queen` |
| Rook contiguity | Polygons where only edge-sharing counts | `libpysal.weights.Rook` |
| KNN | Points, or polygons with islands; fixed neighbor count `k` | `libpysal.weights.KNN` |
| Distance band | Points with meaningful metric distance | `libpysal.weights.DistanceBand` |

## Critical constraints

1. **Always row-standardize** — `w.transform = "r"` before any Moran's I.
2. **Check for islands** — isolated features break Moran's I. Switch to KNN if Queen produces them.
3. **Drop NAs first, then build weights** — weights must align with the rows actually used.
4. **Project before distance-band weights** — distances are meaningless in lat/lon degrees.

## Paths

This skill only reads data — it produces a `w` object, not a file.

- `INPUT_PATH` — GeoPackage/SHP from Input Node Paths. Never hardcode.

## Canonical example

```python
import geopandas as gpd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN, DistanceBand

gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)
col = "<ANALYSIS_COLUMN>"

# ---- 1. Drop NAs on the column you'll analyze ---------------------------
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=[col]).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- 2. Build weights ---------------------------------------------------
# (a) Queen contiguity — default for polygons
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)

# (b) KNN fallback if Queen produces islands
if w.islands:
    print(f"Queen produced {len(w.islands)} islands — switching to KNN(k=5)")
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)

# (c) Distance band — requires projected CRS in meters
# if gdf.crs.is_geographic:
#     gdf = gdf.to_crs(epsg=3857)
# w = DistanceBand.from_dataframe(gdf, threshold=10000, binary=False)

# ---- 3. Row-standardize -------------------------------------------------
w.transform = "r"

print(f"n = {w.n}, mean neighbors = {w.mean_neighbors:.2f}, islands = {len(w.islands)}")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Islands break Moran's I if w.islands: use KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5).
Forgot to row-standardize w.transform = "r" every time.
Weights built before dropping NAs Drop first, reset index, then build — row counts must match.
Distance band in lat/lon Reproject to a meter-based CRS first.
k too small in KNN k=5 to k=8 is typical; too small gives noisy LISA. 
```python
import os

import geopandas as gpd
import pandas as pd
from shapely.geometry import LineString
from libpysal.weights import Queen

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Paths
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_2019_qc.gpkg"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_queen_weights_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Load counties and validate
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
counties = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

required_cols = ["GEOID", "geometry"]
missing = [c for c in required_cols if c not in counties.columns]
if missing:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing required columns: {missing}. Available: {list(counties.columns)}")

# Ensure key is string, drop missing keys
counties["GEOID"] = counties["GEOID"].astype(str)
counties = counties.dropna(subset=["GEOID"]).copy()

# Validate geometry
counties = counties[counties.geometry.notna()].copy()
counties = counties[counties.geometry.is_valid & ~counties.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# Reset index to ensure alignment for weights construction
counties = counties.reset_index(drop=True)

if counties.empty:
    raise ValueError("No valid county geometries remain after validation.")

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Construct Queen contiguity weights keyed by GEOID
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(counties, ids=counties["GEOID"].tolist())
w.transform = "r"  # row-standardize

# Attach neighbor count to polygons for easy inspection
neighbor_counts = pd.Series({k: len(v) for k, v in w.neighbors.items()}, name="queen_nbrs")
counties = counties.merge(neighbor_counts.rename("queen_nbrs"), left_on="GEOID", right_index=True, how="left")
counties["queen_nbrs"] = counties["queen_nbrs"].fillna(0).astype(int)

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Create a spatial "links" layer (LineStrings between centroids)
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Using centroids for visualization/QA; weights themselves are encoded by GEOID pairs.
centroids = counties.set_index("GEOID").geometry.centroid

pairs = []
for i, nbrs in w.neighbors.items():
    for j in nbrs:
        # store each undirected edge once
        if str(i) < str(j):
            pairs.append((str(i), str(j)))

links_records = []
for i, j in pairs:
    if i in centroids.index and j in centroids.index:
        geom = LineString([centroids.loc[i], centroids.loc[j]])
        links_records.append({"GEOID_i": i, "GEOID_j": j, "geometry": geom})

links_gdf = gpd.GeoDataFrame(links_records, geometry="geometry", crs=counties.crs)

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Save to GeoPackage (polygons + queen links)
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
if os.path.exists(OUTPUT_PATH):
    os.remove(OUTPUT_PATH)

counties.to_file(OUTPUT_PATH, layer="counties", driver="GPKG")
links_gdf.to_file(OUTPUT_PATH, layer="queen_links", driver="GPKG")

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
# Record artifact for manuscript pipeline (auto-render choropleth)
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_PATH,
    caption="California county polygons with Queen contiguity summary (neighbor counts) and centroid-to-centroid neighbor links keyed by GEOID.",
    viz_hint={"type": "choropleth", "column": "queen_nbrs", "cmap": "viridis", "scheme": "Quantiles"},
    role="final",
)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=global_morans_i)

# Global Moran's I

## Description

Global Moran's I is a single-number test: **is there overall spatial autocorrelation in this variable?** Positive I means similar values cluster together; negative I means neighbors differ; I near E[I] means random.

## When to use

- Screening a variable for spatial clustering before further spatial analysis.
- Checking **regression residuals** — significant Moran's I on residuals justifies moving from OLS to spatial regression or GWR.
- Comparing clustering strength across multiple variables or time periods.

## When NOT to use

- Locating **where** clusters are → use Local Moran's I (LISA).
- Testing two-variable relationships → bivariate correlation skill.
- Variable with no spatial geometry attached.

## Critical constraints

1. **Build weights on the cleaned GeoDataFrame** — drop NAs first, then `Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)`.
2. **Row-standardize** — `w.transform = "r"`.
3. **Use permutations for inference** — `permutations=999` gives stable p-values; don't rely on the analytical z-score alone.
4. **Prefer KNN if the Queen graph has islands** — see the Spatial Weights skill.

## Paths

- `INPUT_PATH` — GeoPackage/SHP from Input Node Paths.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — CSV with Moran's I statistics (primary result).
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — for any secondary artifacts if added.

Never hardcode `"data.gpkg"`.

## Canonical example (variable + residuals)

```python
import os
import geopandas as gpd
import pandas as pd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from esda.moran import Moran

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH from step I/O section.
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

col = "<TARGET_COLUMN>"          # or a residual column like "gwr_resid"
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=[col]).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- Guard against empty / tiny frames (usually caused by upstream join NaN) ----
if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows after dropping NA in '{col}'. Check upstream join match rates.")
if len(gdf) < 10:
    print(f"[WARN] Only {len(gdf)} rows — spatial statistics will be unreliable.")

# ---- Weights ------------------------------------------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)
if w.islands:
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)
w.transform = "r"

# ---- Global Moran's I ---------------------------------------------------
mi = Moran(gdf[col].values, w, permutations=999)

print(f"Global Moran's I on '{col}':")
print(f"  I          = {mi.I:.4f}")
print(f"  E[I]       = {mi.EI:.4f}")
print(f"  z (sim)    = {mi.z_sim:.4f}")
print(f"  p (sim)    = {mi.p_sim:.6f}")
print("  =>", "significant spatial autocorrelation" if mi.p_sim < 0.05 else "no significant autocorrelation")

# ---- Save ---------------------------------------------------------------
results = pd.DataFrame([{
    "variable": col,
    "morans_I": mi.I,
    "expected_I": mi.EI,
    "variance_sim": mi.VI_sim,
    "z_sim": mi.z_sim,
    "p_sim": mi.p_sim,
    "n": len(gdf),
}])
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
results.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Interpretation

Condition Meaning
I > E[I] and p_sim < 0.05 Positive spatial autocorrelation — clustering of similar values
I ≈ E[I] and p_sim > 0.05 Spatially random
I < E[I] and p_sim < 0.05 Negative spatial autocorrelation — checkerboard/dispersion

E[I] = -1/(n-1) — essentially 0 for large n.

Residual diagnostic: if Moran's I on OLS residuals is significant, OLS is mis-specified spatially → try spatial lag/error regression or GWR.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Weights built on original gdf, analysis on subset Drop NAs first, reset index, then build weights.
Forgot row-standardization w.transform = "r".
Islands in Queen weights Swap in KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5).
Reporting only mi.p_norm Prefer mi.p_sim (permutation-based) — more robust.
Interpreting as "where" Global I tells you whether, not where. Follow up with LISA. 
```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from esda.moran import Moran

# ----------------------------
# Paths (given)
# ----------------------------
COUNTIES_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_2019_qc.gpkg"
WEIGHTS_REF_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_queen_weights_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_NODE_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_global_moransI_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH)

os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ----------------------------
# Load inputs
# ----------------------------
gdf = gpd.read_file(COUNTIES_PATH)
_ = gpd.read_file(WEIGHTS_REF_PATH)  # reference input (not required to compute Queen weights)

target_col = "pm25_mean_2019"

# ----------------------------
# Validate / clean geometry & target values
# ----------------------------
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.notna()]
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=[target_col]).reset_index(drop=True)

if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows available after dropping NA in '{target_col}' and invalid/empty geometries.")
if len(gdf) < 3:
    raise ValueError(f"Need at least 3 observations for Moran's I; got n={len(gdf)}.")

# ----------------------------
# Build Queen contiguity weights (row-standardized), handle islands
# ----------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf, use_index=False)

# If islands exist, fall back to KNN to ensure all observations have neighbors
used_weights = "queen"
if getattr(w, "islands", None):
    if len(w.islands) > 0:
        w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)
        used_weights = "knn_k5_fallback_from_queen_islands"

w.transform = "r"

# ----------------------------
# Global Moran's I (permutation inference)
# ----------------------------
permutations = 999
y = gdf[target_col].to_numpy(dtype=float)

mi = Moran(y, w, permutations=permutations)

results = pd.DataFrame(
    [
        {
            "variable": target_col,
            "weights": used_weights,
            "n": int(len(gdf)),
            "permutations": int(permutations),
            "morans_I": float(mi.I),
            "expected_I": float(mi.EI),
            "variance": float(mi.VI_sim),
            "z_score": float(mi.z_sim),
            "p_value": float(mi.p_sim),
        }
    ]
)

# ----------------------------
# Save primary output
# ----------------------------
results.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

# Also save a manuscript-table copy and register it
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "pm25_global_moransI_2019.csv")
results.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="Global Moran’s I (Queen contiguity; row-standardized) for county-level PM2.5 mean in 2019, reporting permutation-based variance, z-score, and p-value.",
    role="final",
    columns=["variable", "weights", "n", "permutations", "morans_I", "expected_I", "variance", "z_score", "p_value"],
)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=Merging datasets by key (pandas merge) or geometry (geopandas sjoin), section=example)

--- Reading skill doc: 'Merging datasets by key (pandas merge) or geometry (geopandas sjoin)' ---

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# ---- 1. Load ------------------------------------------------------------
left  = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)   # polygons (or a GeoDataFrame)
right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")
right = right.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------
merged = left.merge(right, left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- 5. AUDIT the merge -------------------------------------------------
right_added = [c for c in right.columns if c != RIGHT_KEY and c in merged.columns]
audit_col   = right_added[0] if right_added else None

if audit_col is not None:
    matched      = int(merged[audit_col].notna().sum())
    total        = len(merged)
    match_rate   = matched / total if total else 0.0
    unmatched_n  = total - matched

    audit_lines = [
        f"[JOIN AUDIT] merged {total} left rows",
        f"  matched on '{audit_col}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
        f"  unmatched (NaN in right side): {unmatched_n}",
    ]
    if match_rate < 0.9:
        audit_lines.append(f"  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect keys:")
        audit_lines.append(f"    left  {LEFT_KEY} sample: {left[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        audit_lines.append(f"    right {RIGHT_KEY} sample: {right[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")
    audit = "\n".join(audit_lines)
    print(audit)
    os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    with open(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit.txt"), "w") as f:
        f.write(audit + "\n")

# ---- 6. Save primary output --------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
if isinstance(merged, gpd.GeoDataFrame):
    merged.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")
else:
    merged.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

--- Reading skill doc: 'create FIPS GEOID by zero-padding state_fips county_fips and selecting columns in pandas' ---

Data Merging (Join, Merge, Spatial Join)

Description

Combine two tables by a shared key (pd.merge) or by geometry (gpd.sjoin).
The correctness of every downstream step depends on the match rate — a
silent join that produces NaN for 50% of rows will poison later modeling.

When to use

  • Linking attribute data (CSV) to polygons (GeoPackage/SHP) on FIPS/GEOID.
  • Combining variables from two CSV sources on a shared key.
  • Enriching points/polygons via spatial containment.

When NOT to use

  • Reshape only (pivot/melt) — not a merge.
  • Concatenating rows of identical schema — use pd.concat.

Critical constraints

  1. Always cast join keys to string and zfill to a consistent width
    before merging. Int-vs-string and missing-leading-zero mismatches silently
    drop every match.
  2. State FIPS: zfill(2) (e.g. "06").
  3. County FIPS: zfill(3) (e.g. "001").
  4. County GEOID (state+county): zfill(5) (e.g. "06001").
  5. Tract GEOID: zfill(11).
  6. Strip whitespace on both keys: .astype(str).str.strip().
  7. Replace Census sentinels with NaN on any ACS/Decennial column:
    df.replace(-666666666, np.nan, inplace=True). Values like -999999999,
    -888888888, -666666666 are Census "suppressed / not available" codes
    — not real numbers.
  8. Audit and print match rate after every merge. A match rate below 90%
    is a red flag — either keys are mis-formatted or the right-side dataset
    doesn't cover all left-side units (report both hypotheses).
  9. Left join keeps every left row — NaN on the right side does NOT raise
    an error. You must inspect the output for NaN, not just row count.
  10. For spatial joins, both GeoDataFrames must be in the same projected
    CRS.     Reproject before sjoin.

Paths

  • INPUT_PATH_LEFT, INPUT_PATH_RIGHT — from the step's Input Node Paths.
  • OUTPUT_NODE_PATH — merged primary output.
  • OUTPUT_DIR — directory for join-audit log.

Never hardcode "data.csv", "dataset_a.csv", etc.

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# ---- 1. Load ------------------------------------------------------------
left  = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)   # polygons (or a GeoDataFrame)
right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")
right = right.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------
merged = left.merge(right, left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- 5. AUDIT the merge -------------------------------------------------
right_added = [c for c in right.columns if c != RIGHT_KEY and c in merged.columns]
audit_col   = right_added[0] if right_added else None

if audit_col is not None:
    matched      = int(merged[audit_col].notna().sum())
    total        = len(merged)
    match_rate   = matched / total if total else 0.0
    unmatched_n  = total - matched

    audit_lines = [
        f"[JOIN AUDIT] merged {total} left rows",
        f"  matched on '{audit_col}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
        f"  unmatched (NaN in right side): {unmatched_n}",
    ]
    if match_rate < 0.9:
        audit_lines.append(f"  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect keys:")
        audit_lines.append(f"    left  {LEFT_KEY} sample: {left[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        audit_lines.append(f"    right {RIGHT_KEY} sample: {right[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")
    audit = "\n".join(audit_lines)
    print(audit)
    os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    with open(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit.txt"), "w") as f:
        f.write(audit + "\n")

# ---- 6. Save primary output --------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
if isinstance(merged, gpd.GeoDataFrame):
    merged.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")
else:
    merged.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Spatial join variant (points in polygons)

import geopandas as gpd

points   = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)
polygons = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)

# Reproject to same CRS (use polygons' CRS by convention)
if points.crs != polygons.crs:
    points = points.to_crs(polygons.crs)

joined = gpd.sjoin(points, polygons, how="left", predicate="within")

# Audit — how many points landed in a polygon?
unmatched = joined["index_right"].isna().sum()
print(f"[SJOIN AUDIT] {len(joined)-unmatched}/{len(joined)} points matched a polygon "
      f"({unmatched} outside all polygons)")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Int vs string FIPS silently produces 0 matches Cast both sides to str.strip().str.zfill(W) with the right width.
Leading zeros stripped by pd.read_csv Either dtype={'GEOID': str} at read time, or zfill after load.
ACS sentinel -666666666 treated as a real value df.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan).
"58 records created" looks fine but half are NaN Always print match rate, not just row count.
sjoin returns 0 rows Reproject to a common CRS first; verify with points.within(polygons.unary_union).sum().
how="inner" after a previously-failed join Use how="left" for auditing; switch to inner only after you've verified the match rate.
Duplicated keys on the right side explode left row count right.drop_duplicates(subset=[RIGHT_KEY]) before merge if right is supposed to be unique.
Tract vs county GEOID width mismatch Decide which level the join is at; enforce the matching width on both sides.

--- End skill doc ---

import os
import pandas as pd

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/gini_2019_filtered.csv"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/gini_2019_with_geoid.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH)

# Helpers are pre-imported in the environment:
# record_figure, record_table, record_data_to_viz

# ----------------------------
# Load
# ----------------------------
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH)

# ----------------------------
# Create GEOID (county) = state_fips (2) + county_fips (3)
# ----------------------------
df["state_fips"] = df["state_fips"].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(2)
df["county_fips"] = df["county_fips"].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(3)
df["GEOID"] = df["state_fips"] + df["county_fips"]

# ----------------------------
# Retain only requested columns
# ----------------------------
out = df[["GEOID", "B19083_001E:Gini Index"]].copy()
out["GEOID"] = out["GEOID"].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(5)

# Drop rows where GEOID is missing/invalid after formatting
out = out.dropna(subset=["GEOID"])
out = out.loc[out["GEOID"].str.len() == 5].reset_index(drop=True)

# ----------------------------
# Save
# ----------------------------
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
out.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

Data Merging (Join, Merge, Spatial Join)

Description

Combine two tables by a shared key (pd.merge) or by geometry (gpd.sjoin).
The correctness of every downstream step depends on the match rate — a
silent join that produces NaN for 50% of rows will poison later modeling.

When to use

  • Linking attribute data (CSV) to polygons (GeoPackage/SHP) on FIPS/GEOID.
  • Combining variables from two CSV sources on a shared key.
  • Enriching points/polygons via spatial containment.

When NOT to use

  • Reshape only (pivot/melt) — not a merge.
  • Concatenating rows of identical schema — use pd.concat.

Critical constraints

  1. Always cast join keys to string and zfill to a consistent width
    before merging. Int-vs-string and missing-leading-zero mismatches silently
    drop every match.
  2. State FIPS: zfill(2) (e.g. "06").
  3. County FIPS: zfill(3) (e.g. "001").
  4. County GEOID (state+county): zfill(5) (e.g. "06001").
  5. Tract GEOID: zfill(11).
  6. Strip whitespace on both keys: .astype(str).str.strip().
  7. Replace Census sentinels with NaN on any ACS/Decennial column:
    df.replace(-666666666, np.nan, inplace=True). Values like -999999999,
    -888888888, -666666666 are Census "suppressed / not available" codes
    — not real numbers.
  8. Audit and print match rate after every merge. A match rate below 90%
    is a red flag — either keys are mis-formatted or the right-side dataset
    doesn't cover all left-side units (report both hypotheses).
  9. Left join keeps every left row — NaN on the right side does NOT raise
    an error. You must inspect the output for NaN, not just row count.
  10. For spatial joins, both GeoDataFrames must be in the same projected
    CRS.     Reproject before sjoin.

Paths

  • INPUT_PATH_LEFT, INPUT_PATH_RIGHT — from the step's Input Node Paths.
  • OUTPUT_NODE_PATH — merged primary output.
  • OUTPUT_DIR — directory for join-audit log.

Never hardcode "data.csv", "dataset_a.csv", etc.

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# ---- 1. Load ------------------------------------------------------------
left  = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)   # polygons (or a GeoDataFrame)
right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")
right = right.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------
merged = left.merge(right, left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- 5. AUDIT the merge -------------------------------------------------
right_added = [c for c in right.columns if c != RIGHT_KEY and c in merged.columns]
audit_col   = right_added[0] if right_added else None

if audit_col is not None:
    matched      = int(merged[audit_col].notna().sum())
    total        = len(merged)
    match_rate   = matched / total if total else 0.0
    unmatched_n  = total - matched

    audit_lines = [
        f"[JOIN AUDIT] merged {total} left rows",
        f"  matched on '{audit_col}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
        f"  unmatched (NaN in right side): {unmatched_n}",
    ]
    if match_rate < 0.9:
        audit_lines.append(f"  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect keys:")
        audit_lines.append(f"    left  {LEFT_KEY} sample: {left[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        audit_lines.append(f"    right {RIGHT_KEY} sample: {right[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")
    audit = "\n".join(audit_lines)
    print(audit)
    os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    with open(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit.txt"), "w") as f:
        f.write(audit + "\n")

# ---- 6. Save primary output --------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
if isinstance(merged, gpd.GeoDataFrame):
    merged.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")
else:
    merged.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Spatial join variant (points in polygons)

import geopandas as gpd

points   = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)
polygons = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)

# Reproject to same CRS (use polygons' CRS by convention)
if points.crs != polygons.crs:
    points = points.to_crs(polygons.crs)

joined = gpd.sjoin(points, polygons, how="left", predicate="within")

# Audit — how many points landed in a polygon?
unmatched = joined["index_right"].isna().sum()
print(f"[SJOIN AUDIT] {len(joined)-unmatched}/{len(joined)} points matched a polygon "
      f"({unmatched} outside all polygons)")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Int vs string FIPS silently produces 0 matches Cast both sides to str.strip().str.zfill(W) with the right width.
Leading zeros stripped by pd.read_csv Either dtype={'GEOID': str} at read time, or zfill after load.
ACS sentinel -666666666 treated as a real value df.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan).
"58 records created" looks fine but half are NaN Always print match rate, not just row count.
sjoin returns 0 rows Reproject to a common CRS first; verify with points.within(polygons.unary_union).sum().
how="inner" after a previously-failed join Use how="left" for auditing; switch to inner only after you've verified the match rate.
Duplicated keys on the right side explode left row count right.drop_duplicates(subset=[RIGHT_KEY]) before merge if right is supposed to be unique.
Tract vs county GEOID width mismatch Decide which level the join is at; enforce the matching width on both sides.

--- End skill doc ---

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

INPUT_COUNTIES_GPKG = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_2019_qc.gpkg"
INPUT_GINI_CSV = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/gini_2019_with_geoid.csv"

OUTPUT_GPKG = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019.gpkg"

# ---- Load inputs ----
counties = gpd.read_file(INPUT_COUNTIES_GPKG)
gini = pd.read_csv(INPUT_GINI_CSV)

# ---- Validate required columns (from Step 1 inspection) ----
LEFT_KEY = "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "GEOID"
GINI_COL = "B19083_001E:Gini Index"

missing_left = [c for c in [LEFT_KEY, "geometry"] if c not in counties.columns]
missing_right = [c for c in [RIGHT_KEY, GINI_COL] if c not in gini.columns]
if missing_left:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing columns in counties layer: {missing_left}. Available: {list(counties.columns)}")
if missing_right:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing columns in gini CSV: {missing_right}. Available: {list(gini.columns)}")

# ---- Geometry QC (required) ----
counties = counties[counties.geometry.notna()]
counties = counties[~counties.geometry.is_empty]
counties = counties[counties.geometry.is_valid].copy()

# ---- Normalize join keys ----
# County GEOID is 5 chars (state+county FIPS)
KEY_WIDTH = 5
counties[LEFT_KEY] = counties[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
gini[RIGHT_KEY] = gini[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- Clean/convert Gini column to numeric ----
gini[GINI_COL] = pd.to_numeric(gini[GINI_COL], errors="coerce")
gini = gini.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- Deduplicate right side on join key (defensive) ----
gini = gini.drop_duplicates(subset=[RIGHT_KEY]).copy()

# ---- Left join ----
merged = counties.merge(gini[[RIGHT_KEY, GINI_COL]], left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- Join audit ----
matched = int(merged[GINI_COL].notna().sum())
total = int(len(merged))
match_rate = matched / total if total else 0.0
unmatched = total - matched

audit_lines = [
    "[JOIN AUDIT] counties_pm25_2019_qc.gpkg (left) + gini_2019_with_geoid.csv (right)",
    f"  left rows: {total}",
    f"  matched '{GINI_COL}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
    f"  unmatched (NaN in right): {unmatched}",
]
if match_rate < 0.9:
    audit_lines.append("  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect GEOID formatting/coverage.")
    audit_lines.append(f"    left GEOID sample: {counties[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
    audit_lines.append(f"    right GEOID sample: {gini[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
    audit_lines.append(
        f"    example unmatched left GEOIDs: {merged.loc[merged[GINI_COL].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()}"
    )

audit_text = "\n".join(audit_lines)
print(audit_text)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
audit_path = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit_gini_2019_counties.txt")
with open(audit_path, "w") as f:
    f.write(audit_text + "\n")

# ---- Save output ----
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_GPKG), exist_ok=True)
merged.to_file(OUTPUT_GPKG, driver="GPKG")

# ---- Record artifact for deferred visualization ----
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_GPKG,
    caption="California counties with 2019 PM2.5 mean and 2019 ACS Gini Index joined by GEOID.",
    viz_hint={"type": "choropleth", "column": GINI_COL},
    role="intermediate",
)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=ols regression, section=)

# OLS Regression

## Description

Classical multiple linear regression: `y = β₀ + β₁x₁ + … + βₖxₖ + ε`. Used as the **baseline** before any spatial or local model — always fit OLS first, then decide whether residual diagnostics force you to escalate (GWR, SAR, SEM).

## When to use

- Baseline model before spatial regression / GWR.
- Global, stationary relationships with continuous `y`.
- You need interpretable coefficients with p-values, SEs, R², AIC.

## When NOT to use

- Residuals are spatially autocorrelated → escalate to Spatial Regression (SAR/SEM) or GWR.
- `y` is binary / count → use logistic or Poisson regression.
- Predictors strongly collinear (VIF > 10) → drop, combine, or regularize (Ridge/Lasso).

## Critical constraints

1. **Cast to numeric and drop NAs jointly** across `y` and all `X` — row masks must align.
2. **Add a constant** — statsmodels does **not** add one automatically: `sm.add_constant(X)`.
3. **Check VIF** before trusting individual coefficients. VIF > 10 is a red flag.
4. **Inspect residuals spatially** if the data has geometry — OLS assumes `ε` is independent.
5. **Report n, R², adj-R², AIC, coefficient table** — not just R² in isolation.

## Paths

The canonical example uses three variables the modeling agent substitutes
from its own INPUT / OUTPUT PATHS section. **Never hardcode `"data.csv"`.**

- `INPUT_PATH` — read from the step's **Input Node Paths**. Call
  `list_datasets()` and `get_columns()` first to confirm the file and columns.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — the step's **primary** output path (per-step unique).
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — pre-injected directory for **secondary** artifacts
  (coefficient tables, VIF, diagnostics, plots). Use
  `os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "…")`.

## Canonical example (fit → diagnostics → VIF → spatial residual check)

```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import statsmodels.api as sm
from statsmodels.stats.outliers_influence import variance_inflation_factor

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH substituted from the step's I/O section.
# OUTPUT_DIR is pre-injected by the framework.
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH)

y_col  = "<DEPENDENT_VARIABLE>"
x_cols = ["<PREDICTOR_1>", "<PREDICTOR_2>", "<PREDICTOR_3>"]

# ---- 1. Clean ------------------------------------------------------------
cols = [y_col] + x_cols
for c in cols:
    df[c] = pd.to_numeric(df[c], errors="coerce")
df = df.dropna(subset=cols).reset_index(drop=True)

y = df[y_col].values
X = df[x_cols].values
X = sm.add_constant(X)          # prepends the intercept column

# ---- 2. Fit --------------------------------------------------------------
model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()
print(model.summary())

# ---- 3. Coefficient table ------------------------------------------------
coef_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": ["const"] + x_cols,
    "beta":     model.params,
    "std_err":  model.bse,
    "t":        model.tvalues,
    "p":        model.pvalues,
    "ci_low":   model.conf_int()[:, 0],
    "ci_high":  model.conf_int()[:, 1],
})
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
coef_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "ols_coefficients.csv"), index=False)

# ---- 4. Fit statistics ---------------------------------------------------
stats = pd.DataFrame([{
    "n":        int(model.nobs),
    "k":        len(x_cols),
    "R2":       model.rsquared,
    "adj_R2":   model.rsquared_adj,
    "F":        model.fvalue,
    "F_pvalue": model.f_pvalue,
    "AIC":      model.aic,
    "BIC":      model.bic,
    "RMSE":     float(np.sqrt(np.mean(model.resid ** 2))),
}])
stats.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "ols_fit_stats.csv"), index=False)
print(stats.to_string(index=False))

# ---- 5. VIF (multicollinearity) -----------------------------------------
vif_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": x_cols,
    "VIF": [variance_inflation_factor(X, i + 1) for i in range(len(x_cols))],
})
vif_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "ols_vif.csv"), index=False)
print(vif_df.to_string(index=False))
if (vif_df["VIF"] > 10).any():
    print("WARNING: VIF > 10 — drop or combine collinear predictors.")

# ---- 6. Residuals for downstream spatial diagnostics --------------------
df["ols_fitted"]   = model.fittedvalues
df["ols_residual"] = model.resid
# Primary output → OUTPUT_NODE_PATH (fitted + residuals merged back to input rows)
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
df.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Residual diagnostics → when to escalate

# If the data is spatial, attach residuals to the GeoDataFrame and run Moran's I
# (see global_morans_i_skill). Significant residual autocorrelation means:
#   - OLS coefficients may still be unbiased, but SEs are wrong
#   - Move to SAR / SEM (see spatial_regression_skill)
#     or GWR (see gwr_skill) if effects are non-stationary

Non-spatial residual checks worth running:

  • Normality of residuals — scipy.stats.shapiro(model.resid) or a QQ-plot.
  • Heteroscedasticity — statsmodels.stats.diagnostic.het_breuschpagan.
  • Linearity — plot residuals vs fitted; look for curvature.

Key result attributes

Attribute Meaning
model.params, .bse, .tvalues, .pvalues Coefficients, SE, t, p
model.conf_int() 95% confidence intervals
model.rsquared, .rsquared_adj R² and adjusted R²
model.fvalue, .f_pvalue Overall F-test
model.aic, .bic Information criteria
model.fittedvalues, .resid ŷ and residuals
model.nobs Effective sample size

Interpretation

  • Report for each predictor: β, SE, t, p, 95% CI.
  • adj_R² penalizes extra predictors — use it to compare models with different k.
  • F_pvalue < 0.05: at least one predictor is useful. Doesn't mean all are.
  • A coefficient's sign and magnitude are only trustworthy if VIF is acceptable and residuals are well-behaved.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Forgot sm.add_constant(X) No intercept → biased fit. Always add it for statsmodels.
NaNs silently drop rows differently across columns Build one mask across y + X, then dropna(subset=cols).
High R², high VIF Model fits the training data but coefficients are unstable. Drop or combine collinear predictors.
Reporting R² alone Always pair with adj-R², n, and the coefficient table.
Ignoring residual autocorrelation on geographic data Run Moran's I on residuals; escalate to SAR/SEM or GWR if significant.
Using sklearn LinearRegression when you want inference sklearn gives no SEs / p-values. Use statsmodels for inference, sklearn for prediction pipelines. 
```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd
import statsmodels.api as sm

# -------------------------------
# Paths (per instructions)
# -------------------------------
INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_NODE_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019_olsresid.gpkg"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# -------------------------------
# Load + basic geometry validation
# -------------------------------
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# -------------------------------
# OLS setup
# -------------------------------
y_col = "pm25_mean_2019"
x_col = "B19083_001E:Gini Index"
key_col = "GEOID"

needed = [key_col, y_col, x_col]
missing = [c for c in needed if c not in gdf.columns]
if missing:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing required columns: {missing}. Available: {list(gdf.columns)}")

# Ensure join key is string-like (robustness)
gdf[key_col] = gdf[key_col].astype(str)

# Coerce y/x to numeric and drop rows missing either
gdf[y_col] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[y_col], errors="coerce")
gdf[x_col] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[x_col], errors="coerce")
model_df = gdf[[key_col, y_col, x_col]].dropna(subset=[y_col, x_col]).copy()

if model_df.shape[0] < 3:
    raise ValueError(f"Not enough complete cases to fit OLS after dropping NA: n={model_df.shape[0]}")

y = model_df[y_col].to_numpy()
X = sm.add_constant(model_df[[x_col]].to_numpy())  # intercept + single predictor

# -------------------------------
# Fit OLS
# -------------------------------
ols_model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()

# Fitted values and residuals
model_df["ols_fitted_pm25"] = ols_model.fittedvalues
model_df["ols_residual_pm25"] = ols_model.resid

# -------------------------------
# Append outputs back to full GeoDataFrame keyed by GEOID
# (rows without model data remain NaN for fitted/residual)
# -------------------------------
attach = model_df[[key_col, "ols_fitted_pm25", "ols_residual_pm25"]].copy()
gdf = gdf.merge(attach, on=key_col, how="left", validate="1:1")

# -------------------------------
# Save manuscript-ready coefficient + fit-stat tables
# -------------------------------
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)

coef_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": ["const", x_col],
    "coef": ols_model.params,
    "std_err": ols_model.bse,
    "t": ols_model.tvalues,
    "p_value": ols_model.pvalues,
    "ci_low": ols_model.conf_int()[:, 0],
    "ci_high": ols_model.conf_int()[:, 1],
})
coef_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "ols_pm25_gini_coefficients.csv")
coef_df.to_csv(coef_path, index=False)

fit_stats_df = pd.DataFrame([{
    "n": int(ols_model.nobs),
    "R2": float(ols_model.rsquared),
    "adj_R2": float(ols_model.rsquared_adj),
    "AIC": float(ols_model.aic),
    "BIC": float(ols_model.bic),
    "RMSE": float(np.sqrt(np.mean(np.square(ols_model.resid)))),
}])
fit_stats_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "ols_pm25_gini_fit_stats.csv")
fit_stats_df.to_csv(fit_stats_path, index=False)

# Record tables for manuscript
record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=coef_path,
    caption="OLS coefficients for PM2.5 (2019) regressed on county Gini Index.",
    role="promoted",
    columns=["variable", "coef", "std_err", "p_value", "ci_low", "ci_high"],
)
record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=fit_stats_path,
    caption="OLS fit statistics for PM2.5 (2019) ~ Gini Index model.",
    role="promoted",
    columns=["n", "R2", "adj_R2", "AIC", "BIC", "RMSE"],
)

# -------------------------------
# Save primary output GeoPackage
# -------------------------------
gdf.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")

# Optionally register the output dataset for downstream auto-rendering (not required)
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_NODE_PATH,
    caption="County-level OLS fitted PM2.5 (2019) and residuals from regression on Gini Index.",
    viz_hint={"type": "choropleth", "column": "ols_residual_pm25", "cmap": "RdBu", "scheme": "Quantiles"},
    role="final",
)
