🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=global_morans_i)

# Global Moran's I

## Description

Global Moran's I is a single-number test: **is there overall spatial autocorrelation in this variable?** Positive I means similar values cluster together; negative I means neighbors differ; I near E[I] means random.

## When to use

- Screening a variable for spatial clustering before further spatial analysis.
- Checking **regression residuals** — significant Moran's I on residuals justifies moving from OLS to spatial regression or GWR.
- Comparing clustering strength across multiple variables or time periods.

## When NOT to use

- Locating **where** clusters are → use Local Moran's I (LISA).
- Testing two-variable relationships → bivariate correlation skill.
- Variable with no spatial geometry attached.

## Critical constraints

1. **Build weights on the cleaned GeoDataFrame** — drop NAs first, then `Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)`.
2. **Row-standardize** — `w.transform = "r"`.
3. **Use permutations for inference** — `permutations=999` gives stable p-values; don't rely on the analytical z-score alone.
4. **Prefer KNN if the Queen graph has islands** — see the Spatial Weights skill.

## Paths

- `INPUT_PATH` — GeoPackage/SHP from Input Node Paths.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — CSV with Moran's I statistics (primary result).
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — for any secondary artifacts if added.

Never hardcode `"data.gpkg"`.

## Canonical example (variable + residuals)

```python
import os
import geopandas as gpd
import pandas as pd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from esda.moran import Moran

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH from step I/O section.
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

col = "<TARGET_COLUMN>"          # or a residual column like "gwr_resid"
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=[col]).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- Guard against empty / tiny frames (usually caused by upstream join NaN) ----
if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows after dropping NA in '{col}'. Check upstream join match rates.")
if len(gdf) < 10:
    print(f"[WARN] Only {len(gdf)} rows — spatial statistics will be unreliable.")

# ---- Weights ------------------------------------------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)
if w.islands:
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)
w.transform = "r"

# ---- Global Moran's I ---------------------------------------------------
mi = Moran(gdf[col].values, w, permutations=999)

print(f"Global Moran's I on '{col}':")
print(f"  I          = {mi.I:.4f}")
print(f"  E[I]       = {mi.EI:.4f}")
print(f"  z (sim)    = {mi.z_sim:.4f}")
print(f"  p (sim)    = {mi.p_sim:.6f}")
print("  =>", "significant spatial autocorrelation" if mi.p_sim < 0.05 else "no significant autocorrelation")

# ---- Save ---------------------------------------------------------------
results = pd.DataFrame([{
    "variable": col,
    "morans_I": mi.I,
    "expected_I": mi.EI,
    "variance_sim": mi.VI_sim,
    "z_sim": mi.z_sim,
    "p_sim": mi.p_sim,
    "n": len(gdf),
}])
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
results.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Interpretation

Condition Meaning
I > E[I] and p_sim < 0.05 Positive spatial autocorrelation — clustering of similar values
I ≈ E[I] and p_sim > 0.05 Spatially random
I < E[I] and p_sim < 0.05 Negative spatial autocorrelation — checkerboard/dispersion

E[I] = -1/(n-1) — essentially 0 for large n.

Residual diagnostic: if Moran's I on OLS residuals is significant, OLS is mis-specified spatially → try spatial lag/error regression or GWR.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Weights built on original gdf, analysis on subset Drop NAs first, reset index, then build weights.
Forgot row-standardization w.transform = "r".
Islands in Queen weights Swap in KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5).
Reporting only mi.p_norm Prefer mi.p_sim (permutation-based) — more robust.
Interpreting as "where" Global I tells you whether, not where. Follow up with LISA. 
```python
import os
import warnings

import geopandas as gpd
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
from esda.moran import Moran
from libpysal.weights import Queen

# ---------------------------
# Paths
# ---------------------------
RESID_GPKG = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019_olsresid.gpkg"
WQ_GPKG = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_queen_weights_2019.gpkg"

OUT_CSV = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ols_residuals_moransI_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUT_CSV)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ---------------------------
# Load data
# ---------------------------
resid_gdf = gpd.read_file(RESID_GPKG)
wgeom_gdf = gpd.read_file(WQ_GPKG)

# ---------------------------
# Basic geometry validation
# ---------------------------
resid_gdf = resid_gdf[resid_gdf.geometry.notna()]
resid_gdf = resid_gdf[resid_gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~resid_gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

wgeom_gdf = wgeom_gdf[wgeom_gdf.geometry.notna()]
wgeom_gdf = wgeom_gdf[wgeom_gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~wgeom_gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# ---------------------------
# CRS harmonization (reproject weights geometry to match residuals)
# ---------------------------
if resid_gdf.crs is not None and wgeom_gdf.crs is not None and resid_gdf.crs != wgeom_gdf.crs:
    wgeom_gdf = wgeom_gdf.to_crs(resid_gdf.crs)

# ---------------------------
# Prepare analysis frame keyed by GEOID
# (Use weight geometry as the spatial support; attach residuals by GEOID)
# ---------------------------
resid_df = resid_gdf[["GEOID", "ols_residual_pm25"]].copy()
resid_df["GEOID"] = resid_df["GEOID"].astype(str)
wgeom_gdf = wgeom_gdf.copy()
wgeom_gdf["GEOID"] = wgeom_gdf["GEOID"].astype(str)

gdf = wgeom_gdf.merge(resid_df, on="GEOID", how="left")

# Drop missing residuals (and reset index BEFORE building weights)
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=["ols_residual_pm25"]).reset_index(drop=True)

if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError("No rows available after dropping NA in 'ols_residual_pm25'.")

# Ensure numeric array
y = pd.to_numeric(gdf["ols_residual_pm25"], errors="coerce")
gdf = gdf.assign(ols_residual_pm25=y).dropna(subset=["ols_residual_pm25"]).reset_index(drop=True)
if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError("All values in 'ols_residual_pm25' became NA after numeric coercion.")

# ---------------------------
# Build Queen contiguity weights keyed by GEOID
# ---------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf, ids=gdf["GEOID"].tolist())

# Handle islands while preserving Queen contiguity requirement:
# drop islands and rebuild Queen weights on the remaining units
if getattr(w, "islands", None):
    islands = list(w.islands)
    if len(islands) > 0:
        warnings.warn(
            f"Queen weights contain {len(islands)} island(s). Dropping island GEOID(s) and rebuilding Queen weights."
        )
        gdf = gdf[~gdf["GEOID"].isin(islands)].reset_index(drop=True)
        if len(gdf) == 0:
            raise ValueError("All observations are islands under Queen contiguity; cannot compute Moran's I.")
        w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf, ids=gdf["GEOID"].tolist())

w.transform = "r"

# ---------------------------
# Compute Global Moran's I (permutation inference)
# ---------------------------
mi = Moran(gdf["ols_residual_pm25"].to_numpy(dtype=float), w, permutations=999)

results = pd.DataFrame(
    [
        {
            "variable": "ols_residual_pm25",
            "morans_I": float(mi.I),
            "z_sim": float(mi.z_sim),
            "p_sim": float(mi.p_sim),
            "n": int(len(gdf)),
        }
    ]
)

# Primary output (as specified)
results.to_csv(OUT_CSV, index=False)

# Manuscript table copy (opt-in via tables/ directory) + record
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "ols_residuals_moransI_2019.csv")
results.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="Global Moran’s I (permutation-based) for spatial autocorrelation in OLS residuals of PM2.5 across California counties using Queen contiguity.",
    role="final",
    columns=["variable", "morans_I", "z_sim", "p_sim", "n"],
)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=SPATIAL_REGRESSION: Global spatial regression, section=example)

## Canonical example (OLS → LM tests → SAR or SEM → residual check)

```python
import os
import geopandas as gpd
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from esda.moran import Moran
from spreg import OLS, ML_Lag, ML_Error

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH from the step's I/O section; OUTPUT_DIR pre-injected.
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

y_col  = "<DEPENDENT_VARIABLE>"
x_cols = ["<PREDICTOR_1>", "<PREDICTOR_2>", "<PREDICTOR_3>"]

# ---- 1. Clean & align ---------------------------------------------------
cols = [y_col] + x_cols
for c in cols:
    gdf[c] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[c], errors="coerce")
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=cols).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- Guard against empty / tiny frames (usually caused by upstream join NaN) ----
if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows after dropping NA in {cols}. Check upstream join match rates.")
if len(gdf) < 10:
    print(f"[WARN] Only {len(gdf)} rows — spatial regression will be unreliable.")

y = gdf[[y_col]].values.astype(float)          # (n, 1)
X = gdf[x_cols].values.astype(float)           # (n, k), no intercept

# ---- 2. Weights ---------------------------------------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)
if w.islands:
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)
w.transform = "r"

# ---- 3. OLS baseline with LM diagnostics --------------------------------
ols = OLS(y, X, w=w, spat_diag=True, moran=True, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
print(ols.summary)

lm_lag        = ols.lm_lag           # (stat, p)
lm_error      = ols.lm_error
rlm_lag       = ols.rlm_lag          # robust variants
rlm_error     = ols.rlm_error
print(f"LM-Lag   : stat={lm_lag[0]:.3f}, p={lm_lag[1]:.4f}")
print(f"LM-Error : stat={lm_error[0]:.3f}, p={lm_error[1]:.4f}")
print(f"Robust LM-Lag   : stat={rlm_lag[0]:.3f}, p={rlm_lag[1]:.4f}")
print(f"Robust LM-Error : stat={rlm_error[0]:.3f}, p={rlm_error[1]:.4f}")

# ---- 4. Pick model by LM rule ------------------------------------------
def pick_model(lm_lag, lm_error, rlm_lag, rlm_error, alpha=0.05):
    lag_sig, err_sig = lm_lag[1] < alpha, lm_error[1] < alpha
    if lag_sig and not err_sig: return "lag"
    if err_sig and not lag_sig: return "error"
    if lag_sig and err_sig:
        return "lag" if rlm_lag[1] < rlm_error[1] else "error"
    return "ols"

choice = pick_model(lm_lag, lm_error, rlm_lag, rlm_error)
print(f"LM decision: {choice.upper()}")

# ---- 5. Fit the chosen model -------------------------------------------
if choice == "lag":
    model = ML_Lag(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
    spatial_param = ("rho (ρ)", float(model.rho))
elif choice == "error":
    model = ML_Error(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
    spatial_param = ("lambda (λ)", float(model.lam))
else:
    model = ols
    spatial_param = ("n/a", np.nan)

print(model.summary)
print(f"Spatial parameter {spatial_param[0]} = {spatial_param[1]:.4f}")

# ---- 6. Residual Moran's I (did the model absorb the autocorrelation?) -
resid = np.asarray(model.u).flatten()
mi_resid = Moran(resid, w, permutations=999)
print(f"Residual Moran's I = {mi_resid.I:.4f}, p = {mi_resid.p_sim:.4f}")

# ---- 7. Save fitted values, residuals, coefficients --------------------
out = gdf.copy()
out["fitted"]   = np.asarray(model.predy).flatten()
out["residual"] = resid
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
out.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")

coef_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": ["CONSTANT"] + x_cols,
    "beta":     np.asarray(model.betas).flatten()[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "std_err":  np.asarray(model.std_err).flatten()[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "z":        np.asarray([t[0] for t in model.z_stat])[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "p":        np.asarray([t[1] for t in model.z_stat])[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
})
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
coef_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "spatial_regression_coefficients.csv"), index=False)


🔧 [TOOL CALL] **lookup_skill_doc**(query=SPATIAL_WEIGHTS: Building spatial weights matrices, section=pitfalls)

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Islands break Moran's I if w.islands: use KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5).
Forgot to row-standardize w.transform = "r" every time.
Weights built before dropping NAs Drop first, reset index, then build — row counts must match.
Distance band in lat/lon Reproject to a meter-based CRS first.
k too small in KNN k=5 to k=8 is typical; too small gives noisy LISA. 
```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from spreg import ML_Lag

# Helpers are pre-imported in the environment:
# record_table, record_figure, record_data_to_viz

COUNTIES_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019.gpkg"
WEIGHTS_GPKG_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_queen_weights_2019.gpkg"

OUTPUT_NODE_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/spatial_lag_pm25_on_gini_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH)

y_col = "pm25_mean_2019"
x_col = "B19083_001E:Gini Index"
id_col = "GEOID"

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ----------------------------
# Load inputs
# ----------------------------
gdf = gpd.read_file(COUNTIES_PATH)
wgdf = gpd.read_file(WEIGHTS_GPKG_PATH)

# Validate geometry
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()
wgdf = wgdf[wgdf.geometry.is_valid & ~wgdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# Align CRS (if present on both)
if gdf.crs is not None and wgdf.crs is not None and gdf.crs != wgdf.crs:
    wgdf = wgdf.to_crs(gdf.crs)

# Ensure join key dtype
gdf[id_col] = gdf[id_col].astype(str)
wgdf[id_col] = wgdf[id_col].astype(str)

# Numeric coercion
gdf[y_col] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[y_col], errors="coerce")
gdf[x_col] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[x_col], errors="coerce")

# Keep model columns, drop NAs
model_df = gdf[[id_col, y_col, x_col]].dropna(subset=[y_col, x_col]).copy()

if len(model_df) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows available after dropping NA in [{y_col}, {x_col}].")

# Restrict weights geometry to modeled GEOIDs and ensure unique IDs
keep_ids = model_df[id_col].unique().tolist()
wgdf_sub = wgdf[wgdf[id_col].isin(keep_ids)].copy()
wgdf_sub = wgdf_sub.drop_duplicates(subset=[id_col]).copy()

# Enforce consistent ordering (keyed by GEOID)
model_df = model_df[model_df[id_col].isin(wgdf_sub[id_col])].copy()
model_df = model_df.sort_values(by=id_col).reset_index(drop=True)
wgdf_sub = wgdf_sub[wgdf_sub[id_col].isin(model_df[id_col])].copy()
wgdf_sub = wgdf_sub.sort_values(by=id_col).reset_index(drop=True)

if len(model_df) != len(wgdf_sub):
    raise ValueError(
        f"Row mismatch after GEOID alignment: model_df={len(model_df)}, weights_gdf={len(wgdf_sub)}"
    )
if model_df[id_col].tolist() != wgdf_sub[id_col].tolist():
    raise ValueError("GEOID ordering mismatch between regression data and weights geometry after sorting.")

# ----------------------------
# Build Queen contiguity weights (keyed by GEOID)
# ----------------------------
ids = wgdf_sub[id_col].tolist()
w = Queen.from_dataframe(wgdf_sub, ids=ids)

# Handle islands by switching to KNN (common pitfall)
if getattr(w, "islands", []):
    # Use geometry-based neighbors; KNN requires projected CRS for meaningful distances,
    # but it's used here only as a connectivity fallback for islands.
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(wgdf_sub, k=5, ids=ids)

w.transform = "r"

# ----------------------------
# Fit ML spatial lag (SAR) model
# ----------------------------
y = model_df[[y_col]].values.astype(float)  # (n, 1)
X = model_df[[x_col]].values.astype(float)  # (n, k) without intercept

sar = ML_Lag(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=[x_col])

# ----------------------------
# Assemble output table (parameters + fit stats)
# ----------------------------
betas = np.asarray(sar.betas).flatten().tolist()  # constant + X
rho = float(getattr(sar, "rho", np.nan))
param_names = list(getattr(sar, "name_x", ["CONSTANT", x_col])) + ["rho"]

# Standard errors / z / p: robustly extract, accounting for different spreg versions
std_err_raw = np.asarray(getattr(sar, "std_err", [])).flatten().tolist()
z_stat_raw = getattr(sar, "z_stat", [])

z_vals = []
p_vals = []
for zp in z_stat_raw:
    try:
        z_vals.append(float(zp[0]))
        p_vals.append(float(zp[1]))
    except Exception:
        z_vals.append(np.nan)
        p_vals.append(np.nan)

# Build estimates in the correct order: [betas..., rho]
estimates = betas + [rho]

# Std errors: if rho SE not explicitly present, infer from z-stat if possible
std_err = []
if len(std_err_raw) >= len(estimates):
    std_err = std_err_raw[: len(estimates)]
else:
    std_err = (std_err_raw[: len(betas)] if len(std_err_raw) >= len(betas) else [np.nan] * len(betas))
    # Infer rho SE from z (if the last z corresponds to rho)
    rho_se = np.nan
    if len(z_vals) >= len(estimates):
        z_rho = z_vals[len(estimates) - 1]
        if z_rho not in (0, np.nan) and np.isfinite(z_rho):
            rho_se = rho / z_rho
    std_err = std_err + [rho_se]

# z/p: if lengths mismatch, pad
if len(z_vals) < len(estimates):
    z_vals = z_vals + [np.nan] * (len(estimates) - len(z_vals))
if len(p_vals) < len(estimates):
    p_vals = p_vals + [np.nan] * (len(estimates) - len(p_vals))

coef_df = pd.DataFrame(
    {
        "section": "parameters",
        "variable": param_names,
        "estimate": estimates,
        "std_err": std_err,
        "z_value": z_vals[: len(estimates)],
        "p_value": p_vals[: len(estimates)],
    }
)

fit_items = {
    "n": int(getattr(sar, "n", len(model_df))),
    "k": int(getattr(sar, "k", 1)),
    "log_likelihood": float(getattr(sar, "logll", np.nan)),
    "aic": float(getattr(sar, "aic", np.nan)),
    "bic_schwarz": float(getattr(sar, "schwarz", np.nan)),
    "pseudo_r2": float(getattr(sar, "pr2", np.nan)),
    "sigma2": float(getattr(sar, "sig2", np.nan)),
}
fit_df = pd.DataFrame(
    {"section": ["fit_stats"] * len(fit_items), "variable": list(fit_items.keys()), "estimate": list(fit_items.values())}
)

out_df = pd.concat([coef_df, fit_df], ignore_index=True)

# Primary output (required node path)
out_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

# Manuscript-ready promoted table copy
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "spatial_lag_pm25_on_gini_2019.csv")
out_df.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="Maximum-likelihood spatial lag (SAR) model results for county PM2.5 (2019) regressed on Gini Index with Queen contiguity weights (GEOID-keyed).",
    role="promoted",
    columns=["section", "variable", "estimate", "std_err", "z_value", "p_value"],
)

# Spatial Weights

## Description

A spatial weights matrix `W` defines which observations are neighbors and how strongly they're connected. Almost every spatial statistic (Moran's I, LISA, spatial lag/error regression) takes `W` as input.

## When to use

- Before Global or Local Moran's I.
- Before spatial regression (SAR, SEM) or GWR diagnostics.
- Any time you need to express "neighbor of" relationships between geographic units.

## When NOT to use

- Non-spatial data — no geometry, no weights.
- Purely attribute-space neighborhoods (use sklearn KNN on features instead).

## Choosing the scheme

| Scheme | Use when | Class |
|---|---|---|
| Queen contiguity | Polygons (counties, tracts); neighbors share edge or vertex | `libpysal.weights.Queen` |
| Rook contiguity | Polygons where only edge-sharing counts | `libpysal.weights.Rook` |
| KNN | Points, or polygons with islands; fixed neighbor count `k` | `libpysal.weights.KNN` |
| Distance band | Points with meaningful metric distance | `libpysal.weights.DistanceBand` |

## Critical constraints

1. **Always row-standardize** — `w.transform = "r"` before any Moran's I.
2. **Check for islands** — isolated features break Moran's I. Switch to KNN if Queen produces them.
3. **Drop NAs first, then build weights** — weights must align with the rows actually used.
4. **Project before distance-band weights** — distances are meaningless in lat/lon degrees.

## Paths

This skill only reads data — it produces a `w` object, not a file.

- `INPUT_PATH` — GeoPackage/SHP from Input Node Paths. Never hardcode.

## Canonical example

```python
import geopandas as gpd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN, DistanceBand

gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)
col = "<ANALYSIS_COLUMN>"

# ---- 1. Drop NAs on the column you'll analyze ---------------------------
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=[col]).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- 2. Build weights ---------------------------------------------------
# (a) Queen contiguity — default for polygons
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)

# (b) KNN fallback if Queen produces islands
if w.islands:
    print(f"Queen produced {len(w.islands)} islands — switching to KNN(k=5)")
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)

# (c) Distance band — requires projected CRS in meters
# if gdf.crs.is_geographic:
#     gdf = gdf.to_crs(epsg=3857)
# w = DistanceBand.from_dataframe(gdf, threshold=10000, binary=False)

# ---- 3. Row-standardize -------------------------------------------------
w.transform = "r"

print(f"n = {w.n}, mean neighbors = {w.mean_neighbors:.2f}, islands = {len(w.islands)}")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Islands break Moran's I if w.islands: use KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5).
Forgot to row-standardize w.transform = "r" every time.
Weights built before dropping NAs Drop first, reset index, then build — row counts must match.
Distance band in lat/lon Reproject to a meter-based CRS first.
k too small in KNN k=5 to k=8 is typical; too small gives noisy LISA. 
```python
import os
import warnings

import geopandas as gpd
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
from shapely.geometry import LineString
from libpysal.weights import KNN

# Pre-imported helpers (available in the environment):
# record_data_to_viz

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_knn_weights_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH)

os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# -----------------------------
# Load + validate input geometry
# -----------------------------
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

required_cols = ["GEOID", "geometry"]
missing = [c for c in required_cols if c not in gdf.columns]
if missing:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing required columns: {missing}. Available columns: {list(gdf.columns)}")

gdf["GEOID"] = gdf["GEOID"].astype(str)
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=["GEOID", "geometry"]).copy()
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# Ensure unique IDs (KNN 'ids' must be unique)
dupes = gdf["GEOID"].duplicated()
if dupes.any():
    duped_ids = gdf.loc[dupes, "GEOID"].unique().tolist()
    raise ValueError(f"Duplicate GEOID values found; cannot key weights uniquely. Examples: {duped_ids[:10]}")

gdf = gdf.reset_index(drop=True)

# -----------------------------
# Build centroids in projected CRS
# -----------------------------
source_crs = gdf.crs
if source_crs is None:
    raise ValueError("Input GeoPackage has no CRS; cannot construct distance-based KNN weights reliably.")

# Use a metric CRS for centroid coordinates/distances
if getattr(source_crs, "is_geographic", False):
    metric_epsg = 3857
    gdf_metric = gdf.to_crs(epsg=metric_epsg)
else:
    gdf_metric = gdf.copy()

# Centroids (in metric CRS)
gdf_metric["centroid"] = gdf_metric.geometry.centroid
centroids_metric = gpd.GeoDataFrame(
    gdf_metric[["GEOID"]].copy(),
    geometry=gdf_metric["centroid"],
    crs=gdf_metric.crs,
)

# -----------------------------
# KNN weights (k=5) keyed by GEOID
# -----------------------------
k = 5
n = len(centroids_metric)
if n <= k:
    raise ValueError(f"Not enough observations to build KNN with k={k}. n={n}")

# libpysal KNN uses geometry; ids ensures weights keyed by GEOID
with warnings.catch_warnings():
    warnings.simplefilter("ignore")
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(centroids_metric, k=k, ids=centroids_metric["GEOID"].tolist())

# Row-standardization is common, but output requested is weights construction;
# keep as binary (default) unless you explicitly need standardized weights later.
# w.transform = "r"

# -----------------------------
# Serialize weights as an edges layer (LineStrings between centroids)
# -----------------------------
# Build a centroid lookup for coordinates
centroids_xy = centroids_metric.copy()
centroids_xy["x"] = centroids_xy.geometry.x
centroids_xy["y"] = centroids_xy.geometry.y
xy_lookup = centroids_xy.set_index("GEOID")[["x", "y"]].to_dict(orient="index")

records = []
for origin_id, neigh_ids in w.neighbors.items():
    ox, oy = xy_lookup[origin_id]["x"], xy_lookup[origin_id]["y"]
    for rank, dest_id in enumerate(neigh_ids, start=1):
        dx, dy = xy_lookup[dest_id]["x"], xy_lookup[dest_id]["y"]
        geom = LineString([(ox, oy), (dx, dy)])
        # KNN is typically binary weights=1; keep explicit column
        records.append(
            {
                "origin_id": str(origin_id),
                "dest_id": str(dest_id),
                "rank": int(rank),
                "weight": 1.0,
                "geometry": geom,
            }
        )

edges = gpd.GeoDataFrame(records, geometry="geometry", crs=centroids_metric.crs)

# Also save centroids as a nodes layer (in original CRS for interpretability)
centroids_out = centroids_metric[["GEOID", "geometry"]].copy()
if centroids_out.crs != source_crs:
    centroids_out = centroids_out.to_crs(source_crs)

edges_out = edges.copy()
if edges_out.crs != source_crs:
    edges_out = edges_out.to_crs(source_crs)

# -----------------------------
# Save to GeoPackage (multiple layers)
# -----------------------------
# Overwrite if exists to ensure clean layers
if os.path.exists(OUTPUT_PATH):
    os.remove(OUTPUT_PATH)

centroids_out.to_file(OUTPUT_PATH, layer="centroids", driver="GPKG")
edges_out.to_file(OUTPUT_PATH, layer="knn_edges_k5", driver="GPKG")

# -----------------------------
# Record artifact for manuscript pipeline auto-rendering
# -----------------------------
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_PATH,
    caption="K-nearest-neighbor (k=5) spatial weights for counties, represented as centroid-to-centroid edges keyed by GEOID.",
    viz_hint={"type": "geopackage_layers", "layers": ["centroids", "knn_edges_k5"]},
    role="final",
)

# Spatial Regression (Lag & Error)

## Description

Global regression models that correct for spatial autocorrelation.

- **Spatial Lag (SAR)** — `y = ρWy + Xβ + ε`. Use when the outcome itself *diffuses* across neighbors (crime, prices, disease counts).
- **Spatial Error (SEM)** — `y = Xβ + u, u = λWu + ε`. Use when autocorrelation is a *nuisance* from omitted spatially-structured variables.

## When to use

- OLS residuals show significant Moran's I → global spatial regression is warranted.
- You want **one global** coefficient per predictor, not per-location like GWR.
- Sample size is too small, or relationships too stationary, for GWR.

## When NOT to use

- Coefficients vary across space → use GWR / MGWR.
- No significant residual autocorrelation → plain OLS is fine.
- Very small `n` (< ~50) — ML estimation becomes unstable.

## Choosing Lag vs Error — LM tests

Run OLS first, then Lagrange Multiplier (LM) tests on residuals:

| LM-Lag sig? | LM-Error sig? | Choose |
|---|---|---|
| Yes | No  | Spatial **Lag** |
| No  | Yes | Spatial **Error** |
| Both sig | — | Compare **robust** LM-Lag vs robust LM-Error; pick the more significant |
| Neither | — | Stick with OLS |

## Critical constraints

1. **Build weights on the cleaned frame** — drop NAs, reset index, then `Queen.from_dataframe`.
2. **Row-standardize** — `w.transform = "r"`.
3. **`y` must be 2-D `(n, 1)`** — `gdf[[y_col]].values`, not `gdf[y_col].values`.
4. **No intercept column in `X`** — `spreg` adds it.
5. **Check residual Moran's I after fitting** — if still significant, model is under-specified.
6. **Report ρ (lag) or λ (error)** — these are *the* parameters that justify using the model.

## Paths

Use the three conventional variables from the step's INPUT / OUTPUT PATHS
section — **never hardcode filenames.**

- `INPUT_PATH` — input GeoPackage / CSV from Input Node Paths.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — primary GPKG/CSV with fitted + residuals.
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — directory for the coefficient CSV and any diagnostics.

## Canonical example (OLS → LM tests → SAR or SEM → residual check)

```python
import os
import geopandas as gpd
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from esda.moran import Moran
from spreg import OLS, ML_Lag, ML_Error

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH from the step's I/O section; OUTPUT_DIR pre-injected.
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

y_col  = "<DEPENDENT_VARIABLE>"
x_cols = ["<PREDICTOR_1>", "<PREDICTOR_2>", "<PREDICTOR_3>"]

# ---- 1. Clean & align ---------------------------------------------------
cols = [y_col] + x_cols
for c in cols:
    gdf[c] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[c], errors="coerce")
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=cols).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- Guard against empty / tiny frames (usually caused by upstream join NaN) ----
if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows after dropping NA in {cols}. Check upstream join match rates.")
if len(gdf) < 10:
    print(f"[WARN] Only {len(gdf)} rows — spatial regression will be unreliable.")

y = gdf[[y_col]].values.astype(float)          # (n, 1)
X = gdf[x_cols].values.astype(float)           # (n, k), no intercept

# ---- 2. Weights ---------------------------------------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)
if w.islands:
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)
w.transform = "r"

# ---- 3. OLS baseline with LM diagnostics --------------------------------
ols = OLS(y, X, w=w, spat_diag=True, moran=True, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
print(ols.summary)

lm_lag        = ols.lm_lag           # (stat, p)
lm_error      = ols.lm_error
rlm_lag       = ols.rlm_lag          # robust variants
rlm_error     = ols.rlm_error
print(f"LM-Lag   : stat={lm_lag[0]:.3f}, p={lm_lag[1]:.4f}")
print(f"LM-Error : stat={lm_error[0]:.3f}, p={lm_error[1]:.4f}")
print(f"Robust LM-Lag   : stat={rlm_lag[0]:.3f}, p={rlm_lag[1]:.4f}")
print(f"Robust LM-Error : stat={rlm_error[0]:.3f}, p={rlm_error[1]:.4f}")

# ---- 4. Pick model by LM rule ------------------------------------------
def pick_model(lm_lag, lm_error, rlm_lag, rlm_error, alpha=0.05):
    lag_sig, err_sig = lm_lag[1] < alpha, lm_error[1] < alpha
    if lag_sig and not err_sig: return "lag"
    if err_sig and not lag_sig: return "error"
    if lag_sig and err_sig:
        return "lag" if rlm_lag[1] < rlm_error[1] else "error"
    return "ols"

choice = pick_model(lm_lag, lm_error, rlm_lag, rlm_error)
print(f"LM decision: {choice.upper()}")

# ---- 5. Fit the chosen model -------------------------------------------
if choice == "lag":
    model = ML_Lag(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
    spatial_param = ("rho (ρ)", float(model.rho))
elif choice == "error":
    model = ML_Error(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
    spatial_param = ("lambda (λ)", float(model.lam))
else:
    model = ols
    spatial_param = ("n/a", np.nan)

print(model.summary)
print(f"Spatial parameter {spatial_param[0]} = {spatial_param[1]:.4f}")

# ---- 6. Residual Moran's I (did the model absorb the autocorrelation?) -
resid = np.asarray(model.u).flatten()
mi_resid = Moran(resid, w, permutations=999)
print(f"Residual Moran's I = {mi_resid.I:.4f}, p = {mi_resid.p_sim:.4f}")

# ---- 7. Save fitted values, residuals, coefficients --------------------
out = gdf.copy()
out["fitted"]   = np.asarray(model.predy).flatten()
out["residual"] = resid
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
out.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")

coef_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": ["CONSTANT"] + x_cols,
    "beta":     np.asarray(model.betas).flatten()[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "std_err":  np.asarray(model.std_err).flatten()[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "z":        np.asarray([t[0] for t in model.z_stat])[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "p":        np.asarray([t[1] for t in model.z_stat])[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
})
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
coef_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "spatial_regression_coefficients.csv"), index=False)

Key result attributes

Model Attribute Meaning
OLS ols.lm_lag, ols.lm_error (statistic, p-value) of LM tests
OLS ols.rlm_lag, ols.rlm_error Robust LM variants
SAR model.rho Spatial autoregressive parameter ρ
SEM model.lam Spatial error parameter λ
both model.betas, model.std_err, model.z_stat Coefficients, SE, (z, p)
both model.predy, model.u Fitted values, residuals
both model.pr2, model.aic, model.schwarz Pseudo-R², AIC, BIC

Interpretation

  • ρ > 0 (SAR): high y at a location raises y at its neighbors — positive spillover.
  • λ > 0 (SEM): unobserved shocks are spatially correlated; coefficients are still unbiased, but OLS SEs were wrong.
  • Coefficients in SAR are not marginal effects. Use spreg.diagnostics_sp or compute direct / indirect / total impacts for full interpretation.
  • After fitting, residual Moran's I should be non-significant. If it isn't, try MGWR, a mixed SAR-SEM (SARAR), or revisit predictors.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Added intercept column to X spreg adds it — don't prepend ones.
y is 1-D gdf[[col]].values, not gdf[col].values.
Weights built on raw gdf before dropna Drop NAs, reset index, then build weights.
Interpreting SAR β as OLS β In SAR, effects propagate through W; compute impacts for marginal effects.
Using LM results without checking robust LM when both are significant Always fall back to the robust LM pair when the standard pair is jointly significant.
Residual Moran's I still significant Model under-specified — consider SARAR, GWR, or additional spatial predictors. 
```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

from libpysal.weights import KNN
from esda.moran import Moran
from spreg import ML_Error

# Pre-imported helpers assumed available in this environment:
# record_table, record_figure, record_data_to_viz

INPUT_COUNTIES_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019.gpkg"
INPUT_WEIGHTS_GEOM_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_knn_weights_2019.gpkg"

OUTPUT_NODE_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/spatial_error_pm25_on_gini_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# -----------------------------
# Load inputs
# -----------------------------
counties = gpd.read_file(INPUT_COUNTIES_PATH)
wgeom = gpd.read_file(INPUT_WEIGHTS_GEOM_PATH)

# Validate geometry before spatial operations
counties = counties[counties.geometry.is_valid & ~counties.geometry.is_empty].copy()
wgeom = wgeom[wgeom.geometry.is_valid & ~wgeom.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# Ensure join key dtype consistency
counties["GEOID"] = counties["GEOID"].astype(str)
wgeom["GEOID"] = wgeom["GEOID"].astype(str)

# Reproject to common CRS (use counties as primary)
if counties.crs is not None and wgeom.crs is not None and counties.crs != wgeom.crs:
    wgeom = wgeom.to_crs(counties.crs)

y_col = "pm25_mean_2019"
x_col = "B19083_001E:Gini Index"

# Coerce to numeric and drop missing
for c in [y_col, x_col]:
    counties[c] = pd.to_numeric(counties[c], errors="coerce")

# Align to weights geometry by GEOID (keyed by GEOID)
# Keep only counties present in the weights geometry layer, and order exactly like wgeom
wgeom_keyed = wgeom[["GEOID", "geometry"]].drop_duplicates(subset=["GEOID"]).copy()

data = counties[["GEOID", y_col, x_col]].copy()
data = data.dropna(subset=[y_col, x_col]).copy()

aligned = wgeom_keyed.merge(data, on="GEOID", how="inner")
aligned = aligned.reset_index(drop=True)

if len(aligned) == 0:
    raise ValueError(
        "No rows available after aligning on GEOID and dropping NA for required variables."
    )
if len(aligned) <= 5:
    raise ValueError(
        f"Need more than k=5 observations to build KNN weights; got n={len(aligned)}."
    )

# -----------------------------
# Build KNN weights (k=5), keyed by GEOID
# -----------------------------
# Use ids to ensure the weights object is keyed by GEOID and matches the aligned order
ids = aligned["GEOID"].tolist()
w = KNN.from_dataframe(aligned, k=5, ids=ids)
w.transform = "r"

# -----------------------------
# Fit maximum-likelihood Spatial Error Model (SEM)
# -----------------------------
y = aligned[[y_col]].values.astype(float)          # (n, 1)
X = aligned[[x_col]].values.astype(float)          # (n, 1) no intercept; spreg adds it

model = ML_Error(
    y=y,
    x=X,
    w=w,
    name_y=y_col,
    name_x=[x_col],
)

# -----------------------------
# Extract results into a manuscript-ready table
# -----------------------------
# Coefficients: betas includes [CONSTANT, x...]
betas = np.asarray(model.betas).flatten()
std_err = np.asarray(model.std_err).flatten()

# z_stat is list of tuples (z, p) for coefficients only (incl constant)
z_list = np.asarray([t[0] for t in model.z_stat], dtype=float)
p_list = np.asarray([t[1] for t in model.z_stat], dtype=float)

coef_vars = ["CONSTANT", x_col]
coef_df = pd.DataFrame(
    {
        "variable": coef_vars,
        "coef": betas[: len(coef_vars)],
        "std_err": std_err[: len(coef_vars)],
        "z_value": z_list[: len(coef_vars)],
        "p_value": p_list[: len(coef_vars)],
    }
)

# Model-level diagnostics / fit stats
n = int(model.n)
k = int(model.k)  # includes constant
diag = {
    "n": n,
    "k": k,
    "lambda": float(model.lam),
    "log_likelihood": float(model.logll),
    "aic": float(model.aic),
    "bic": float(model.schwarz),
    "pseudo_r2": float(model.pr2) if getattr(model, "pr2", None) is not None else np.nan,
}

diag_df = pd.DataFrame([diag])

# Optional: residual Moran's I diagnostic (saved as intermediate)
resid = np.asarray(model.u).flatten()
mi = Moran(resid, w, permutations=999)
resid_diag_df = pd.DataFrame(
    [{
        "residual_morans_I": float(mi.I),
        "residual_morans_p_sim": float(mi.p_sim),
        "residual_morans_z_sim": float(mi.z_sim),
        "permutations": int(mi.permutations),
    }]
)

# Combine into one output table (requested output node)
# Repeat model-level stats on each coefficient row for a single flat table.
out_df = coef_df.copy()
for key, val in diag.items():
    out_df[key] = val

# Save primary output
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
out_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

# Save promoted manuscript table copy
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "spatial_error_pm25_on_gini_2019.csv")
out_df.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="Spatial error (SEM) maximum-likelihood estimates for PM2.5 (2019) regressed on county Gini Index (KNN k=5 weights, keyed by GEOID).",
    role="final",
    columns=["variable", "coef", "std_err", "z_value", "p_value", "lambda", "aic", "bic", "log_likelihood", "pseudo_r2", "n", "k"],
)

# Save intermediate residual spatial autocorrelation diagnostic
resid_diag_path = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "sem_residual_moransI_diagnostic.csv")
resid_diag_df.to_csv(resid_diag_path, index=False)

Code generated and saved to /bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/generated_code/op_spatial_error_model_maximum_li_eeaef606.py

🔧 [TOOL CALL] get_columns(file_path=/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput/California_UrbanRural_Classification_2019.csv)

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=pandas create GEOID from FIPS zero pad keep selected columns to csv)

--- Reading skill doc: 'pandas create GEOID from FIPS zero pad keep selected columns to csv' ---

Data Merging (Join, Merge, Spatial Join)

Description

Combine two tables by a shared key (pd.merge) or by geometry (gpd.sjoin).
The correctness of every downstream step depends on the match rate — a
silent join that produces NaN for 50% of rows will poison later modeling.

When to use

  • Linking attribute data (CSV) to polygons (GeoPackage/SHP) on FIPS/GEOID.
  • Combining variables from two CSV sources on a shared key.
  • Enriching points/polygons via spatial containment.

When NOT to use

  • Reshape only (pivot/melt) — not a merge.
  • Concatenating rows of identical schema — use pd.concat.

Critical constraints

  1. Always cast join keys to string and zfill to a consistent width
    before merging. Int-vs-string and missing-leading-zero mismatches silently
    drop every match.
  2. State FIPS: zfill(2) (e.g. "06").
  3. County FIPS: zfill(3) (e.g. "001").
  4. County GEOID (state+county): zfill(5) (e.g. "06001").
  5. Tract GEOID: zfill(11).
  6. Strip whitespace on both keys: .astype(str).str.strip().
  7. Replace Census sentinels with NaN on any ACS/Decennial column:
    df.replace(-666666666, np.nan, inplace=True). Values like -999999999,
    -888888888, -666666666 are Census "suppressed / not available" codes
    — not real numbers.
  8. Audit and print match rate after every merge. A match rate below 90%
    is a red flag — either keys are mis-formatted or the right-side dataset
    doesn't cover all left-side units (report both hypotheses).
  9. Left join keeps every left row — NaN on the right side does NOT raise
    an error. You must inspect the output for NaN, not just row count.
  10. For spatial joins, both GeoDataFrames must be in the same projected
    CRS.     Reproject before sjoin.

Paths

  • INPUT_PATH_LEFT, INPUT_PATH_RIGHT — from the step's Input Node Paths.
  • OUTPUT_NODE_PATH — merged primary output.
  • OUTPUT_DIR — directory for join-audit log.

Never hardcode "data.csv", "dataset_a.csv", etc.

Canonical example (CSV → GeoPackage left join on GEOID, with audit)

import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

# ---- 1. Load ------------------------------------------------------------
left  = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)   # polygons (or a GeoDataFrame)
right = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)    # attribute CSV

LEFT_KEY  = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_LEFT>"     # e.g. "GEOID"
RIGHT_KEY = "<GEOID_COLUMN_ON_RIGHT>"    # e.g. "GEOID"
KEY_WIDTH = 5                            # 2=state, 3=county, 5=county-GEOID, 11=tract

# ---- 2. Normalize join keys on BOTH sides -------------------------------
left[LEFT_KEY]   = left[LEFT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)
right[RIGHT_KEY] = right[RIGHT_KEY].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(KEY_WIDTH)

# ---- 3. Clean Census sentinels on the right side ------------------------
for col in right.select_dtypes(include=["number", "object"]).columns:
    right[col] = pd.to_numeric(right[col], errors="ignore")
right = right.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan)

# ---- 4. Left join -------------------------------------------------------
merged = left.merge(right, left_on=LEFT_KEY, right_on=RIGHT_KEY, how="left")

# ---- 5. AUDIT the merge -------------------------------------------------
right_added = [c for c in right.columns if c != RIGHT_KEY and c in merged.columns]
audit_col   = right_added[0] if right_added else None

if audit_col is not None:
    matched      = int(merged[audit_col].notna().sum())
    total        = len(merged)
    match_rate   = matched / total if total else 0.0
    unmatched_n  = total - matched

    audit_lines = [
        f"[JOIN AUDIT] merged {total} left rows",
        f"  matched on '{audit_col}': {matched}/{total} ({match_rate:.1%})",
        f"  unmatched (NaN in right side): {unmatched_n}",
    ]
    if match_rate < 0.9:
        audit_lines.append(f"  WARNING: match rate below 90% — inspect keys:")
        audit_lines.append(f"    left  {LEFT_KEY} sample: {left[LEFT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        audit_lines.append(f"    right {RIGHT_KEY} sample: {right[RIGHT_KEY].head(5).tolist()}")
        missing = merged.loc[merged[audit_col].isna(), LEFT_KEY].head(10).tolist()
        audit_lines.append(f"    example unmatched left keys: {missing}")
    audit = "\n".join(audit_lines)
    print(audit)
    os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
    with open(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "join_audit.txt"), "w") as f:
        f.write(audit + "\n")

# ---- 6. Save primary output --------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
if isinstance(merged, gpd.GeoDataFrame):
    merged.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")
else:
    merged.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Spatial join variant (points in polygons)

import geopandas as gpd

points   = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_LEFT)
polygons = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH_RIGHT)

# Reproject to same CRS (use polygons' CRS by convention)
if points.crs != polygons.crs:
    points = points.to_crs(polygons.crs)

joined = gpd.sjoin(points, polygons, how="left", predicate="within")

# Audit — how many points landed in a polygon?
unmatched = joined["index_right"].isna().sum()
print(f"[SJOIN AUDIT] {len(joined)-unmatched}/{len(joined)} points matched a polygon "
      f"({unmatched} outside all polygons)")

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Int vs string FIPS silently produces 0 matches Cast both sides to str.strip().str.zfill(W) with the right width.
Leading zeros stripped by pd.read_csv Either dtype={'GEOID': str} at read time, or zfill after load.
ACS sentinel -666666666 treated as a real value df.replace([-666666666, -888888888, -999999999], np.nan).
"58 records created" looks fine but half are NaN Always print match rate, not just row count.
sjoin returns 0 rows Reproject to a common CRS first; verify with points.within(polygons.unary_union).sum().
how="inner" after a previously-failed join Use how="left" for auditing; switch to inner only after you've verified the match rate.
Duplicated keys on the right side explode left row count right.drop_duplicates(subset=[RIGHT_KEY]) before merge if right is supposed to be unique.
Tract vs county GEOID width mismatch Decide which level the join is at; enforce the matching width on both sides.

import os
import pandas as pd

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/outputs/DataRetrieverOutput/California_UrbanRural_Classification_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/urban_rural_with_geoid.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH)

# --- Load -----------------------------------------------------------------
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH)

# --- Create GEOID (county GEOID: 5-char, zero-padded) ---------------------
if "FIPSTXT" not in df.columns:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing required column 'FIPSTXT'. Available columns: {list(df.columns)}")

df["GEOID"] = df["FIPSTXT"].astype(str).str.strip().str.zfill(5)

# --- Keep only requested fields ------------------------------------------
keep_cols = ["GEOID", "Metro2013", "Nonmetro2013", "RuralUrbanContinuumCode2013"]
missing = [c for c in keep_cols if c not in df.columns]
if missing:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing required columns: {missing}. Available columns: {list(df.columns)}")

out_df = df[keep_cols].copy()

# --- Save -----------------------------------------------------------------
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
out_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

# Manuscript artifact logging (intermediate dataset)
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_PATH,
    caption="County-level urban–rural classification fields with standardized 5-character county GEOID.",
    viz_hint={"type": "table"},
    role="intermediate",
)

import os

import geopandas as gpd
import pandas as pd

# ---------------------------
# Paths (fixed by workflow)
# ---------------------------
COUNTIES_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_2019.gpkg"
URBAN_RURAL_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/urban_rural_with_geoid.csv"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_urbanrural_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)

# ---------------------------
# Load inputs
# ---------------------------
counties_gdf = gpd.read_file(COUNTIES_PATH)
urban_df = pd.read_csv(URBAN_RURAL_PATH, dtype={"GEOID": "string"})

# ---------------------------
# Basic geometry validity cleanup (no spatial ops, but keep pipeline robust)
# ---------------------------
if "geometry" in counties_gdf.columns:
    counties_gdf = counties_gdf[counties_gdf.geometry.notnull()]
    counties_gdf = counties_gdf[counties_gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~counties_gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# ---------------------------
# Prepare join keys + right-side columns
# ---------------------------
# Ensure join keys are comparable (string, stripped)
counties_gdf["GEOID"] = counties_gdf["GEOID"].astype("string").str.strip()
urban_df["GEOID"] = urban_df["GEOID"].astype("string").str.strip()

# Only keep required attribute from right table for this operation
urban_keep = urban_df[["GEOID", "Metro2013"]].copy()

# Avoid row explosions if right side has unexpected duplicates
urban_keep = urban_keep.drop_duplicates(subset=["GEOID"])

# ---------------------------
# Left join: attach Metro2013 to counties
# ---------------------------
out_gdf = counties_gdf.merge(urban_keep, on="GEOID", how="left", validate="1:1")

# ---------------------------
# Save output
# ---------------------------
# Keep same CRS; GeoPackage driver preserves geometry + attributes
out_gdf.to_file(OUTPUT_PATH, driver="GPKG")

# ---------------------------
# Record as data-to-viz (optional auto-render)
# ---------------------------
record_data_to_viz(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=OUTPUT_PATH,
    caption="California county polygons with PM2.5 mean (2019), Gini Index, and Metro2013 classification attached via GEOID.",
    viz_hint={"type": "choropleth", "column": "Metro2013"},
    role="intermediate",
)

import os

import geopandas as gpd

🔧 [TOOL CALL] lookup_skill_doc(query=ols regression, section=)

# OLS Regression

## Description

Classical multiple linear regression: `y = β₀ + β₁x₁ + … + βₖxₖ + ε`. Used as the **baseline** before any spatial or local model — always fit OLS first, then decide whether residual diagnostics force you to escalate (GWR, SAR, SEM).

## When to use

- Baseline model before spatial regression / GWR.
- Global, stationary relationships with continuous `y`.
- You need interpretable coefficients with p-values, SEs, R², AIC.

## When NOT to use

- Residuals are spatially autocorrelated → escalate to Spatial Regression (SAR/SEM) or GWR.
- `y` is binary / count → use logistic or Poisson regression.
- Predictors strongly collinear (VIF > 10) → drop, combine, or regularize (Ridge/Lasso).

## Critical constraints

1. **Cast to numeric and drop NAs jointly** across `y` and all `X` — row masks must align.
2. **Add a constant** — statsmodels does **not** add one automatically: `sm.add_constant(X)`.
3. **Check VIF** before trusting individual coefficients. VIF > 10 is a red flag.
4. **Inspect residuals spatially** if the data has geometry — OLS assumes `ε` is independent.
5. **Report n, R², adj-R², AIC, coefficient table** — not just R² in isolation.

## Paths

The canonical example uses three variables the modeling agent substitutes
from its own INPUT / OUTPUT PATHS section. **Never hardcode `"data.csv"`.**

- `INPUT_PATH` — read from the step's **Input Node Paths**. Call
  `list_datasets()` and `get_columns()` first to confirm the file and columns.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — the step's **primary** output path (per-step unique).
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — pre-injected directory for **secondary** artifacts
  (coefficient tables, VIF, diagnostics, plots). Use
  `os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "…")`.

## Canonical example (fit → diagnostics → VIF → spatial residual check)

```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import statsmodels.api as sm
from statsmodels.stats.outliers_influence import variance_inflation_factor

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH substituted from the step's I/O section.
# OUTPUT_DIR is pre-injected by the framework.
df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH)

y_col  = "<DEPENDENT_VARIABLE>"
x_cols = ["<PREDICTOR_1>", "<PREDICTOR_2>", "<PREDICTOR_3>"]

# ---- 1. Clean ------------------------------------------------------------
cols = [y_col] + x_cols
for c in cols:
    df[c] = pd.to_numeric(df[c], errors="coerce")
df = df.dropna(subset=cols).reset_index(drop=True)

y = df[y_col].values
X = df[x_cols].values
X = sm.add_constant(X)          # prepends the intercept column

# ---- 2. Fit --------------------------------------------------------------
model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()
print(model.summary())

# ---- 3. Coefficient table ------------------------------------------------
coef_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": ["const"] + x_cols,
    "beta":     model.params,
    "std_err":  model.bse,
    "t":        model.tvalues,
    "p":        model.pvalues,
    "ci_low":   model.conf_int()[:, 0],
    "ci_high":  model.conf_int()[:, 1],
})
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
coef_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "ols_coefficients.csv"), index=False)

# ---- 4. Fit statistics ---------------------------------------------------
stats = pd.DataFrame([{
    "n":        int(model.nobs),
    "k":        len(x_cols),
    "R2":       model.rsquared,
    "adj_R2":   model.rsquared_adj,
    "F":        model.fvalue,
    "F_pvalue": model.f_pvalue,
    "AIC":      model.aic,
    "BIC":      model.bic,
    "RMSE":     float(np.sqrt(np.mean(model.resid ** 2))),
}])
stats.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "ols_fit_stats.csv"), index=False)
print(stats.to_string(index=False))

# ---- 5. VIF (multicollinearity) -----------------------------------------
vif_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": x_cols,
    "VIF": [variance_inflation_factor(X, i + 1) for i in range(len(x_cols))],
})
vif_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "ols_vif.csv"), index=False)
print(vif_df.to_string(index=False))
if (vif_df["VIF"] > 10).any():
    print("WARNING: VIF > 10 — drop or combine collinear predictors.")

# ---- 6. Residuals for downstream spatial diagnostics --------------------
df["ols_fitted"]   = model.fittedvalues
df["ols_residual"] = model.resid
# Primary output → OUTPUT_NODE_PATH (fitted + residuals merged back to input rows)
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
df.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Residual diagnostics → when to escalate

# If the data is spatial, attach residuals to the GeoDataFrame and run Moran's I
# (see global_morans_i_skill). Significant residual autocorrelation means:
#   - OLS coefficients may still be unbiased, but SEs are wrong
#   - Move to SAR / SEM (see spatial_regression_skill)
#     or GWR (see gwr_skill) if effects are non-stationary

Non-spatial residual checks worth running:

  • Normality of residuals — scipy.stats.shapiro(model.resid) or a QQ-plot.
  • Heteroscedasticity — statsmodels.stats.diagnostic.het_breuschpagan.
  • Linearity — plot residuals vs fitted; look for curvature.

Key result attributes

Attribute Meaning
model.params, .bse, .tvalues, .pvalues Coefficients, SE, t, p
model.conf_int() 95% confidence intervals
model.rsquared, .rsquared_adj R² and adjusted R²
model.fvalue, .f_pvalue Overall F-test
model.aic, .bic Information criteria
model.fittedvalues, .resid ŷ and residuals
model.nobs Effective sample size

Interpretation

  • Report for each predictor: β, SE, t, p, 95% CI.
  • adj_R² penalizes extra predictors — use it to compare models with different k.
  • F_pvalue < 0.05: at least one predictor is useful. Doesn't mean all are.
  • A coefficient's sign and magnitude are only trustworthy if VIF is acceptable and residuals are well-behaved.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Forgot sm.add_constant(X) No intercept → biased fit. Always add it for statsmodels.
NaNs silently drop rows differently across columns Build one mask across y + X, then dropna(subset=cols).
High R², high VIF Model fits the training data but coefficients are unstable. Drop or combine collinear predictors.
Reporting R² alone Always pair with adj-R², n, and the coefficient table.
Ignoring residual autocorrelation on geographic data Run Moran's I on residuals; escalate to SAR/SEM or GWR if significant.
Using sklearn LinearRegression when you want inference sklearn gives no SEs / p-values. Use statsmodels for inference, sklearn for prediction pipelines. 
```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd
import statsmodels.api as sm

# Pre-imported helper (provided by the system)
# record_table(...)

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_urbanrural_interaction_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ols_pm25_gini_metro_interaction_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH)

# -----------------------------
# 1) Load & basic geometry QA
# -----------------------------
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.notnull()]
gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

y_col = "pm25_mean_2019"
x_cols = ["B19083_001E:Gini Index", "Metro2013", "gini_x_metro"]

# Ensure numeric types for modeling
for c in [y_col] + x_cols:
    gdf[c] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[c], errors="coerce")

df = gdf.dropna(subset=[y_col] + x_cols).copy()

# -----------------------------
# 2) Fit OLS
# -----------------------------
y = df[y_col].values.astype(float)
X = df[x_cols].values.astype(float)
X = sm.add_constant(X, has_constant="add")

model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()

# -----------------------------
# 3) Coefficient table (coef, SE, p-value)
# -----------------------------
conf_int = model.conf_int()
coef_df = pd.DataFrame(
    {
        "variable": ["const"] + x_cols,
        "coef": model.params,
        "std_err": model.bse,
        "p_value": model.pvalues,
        "ci_low_95": conf_int[:, 0],
        "ci_high_95": conf_int[:, 1],
    }
)

# Primary output (as requested)
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)
coef_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

# Manuscript-ready table artifact
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "ols_pm25_gini_metro_interaction_2019_coefficients.csv")
coef_df.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="OLS coefficient table for PM2.5 (2019) regressed on Gini Index, Metro2013, and their interaction (gini_x_metro).",
    role="promoted",
    columns=["variable", "coef", "std_err", "p_value", "ci_low_95", "ci_high_95"],
)

# Optional: print summary to logs for traceability
print(model.summary())
print("\nSaved primary coefficients table to:", OUTPUT_PATH)
print("Saved manuscript-ready coefficients table to:", table_path)

# Spatial Regression (Lag & Error)

## Description

Global regression models that correct for spatial autocorrelation.

- **Spatial Lag (SAR)** — `y = ρWy + Xβ + ε`. Use when the outcome itself *diffuses* across neighbors (crime, prices, disease counts).
- **Spatial Error (SEM)** — `y = Xβ + u, u = λWu + ε`. Use when autocorrelation is a *nuisance* from omitted spatially-structured variables.

## When to use

- OLS residuals show significant Moran's I → global spatial regression is warranted.
- You want **one global** coefficient per predictor, not per-location like GWR.
- Sample size is too small, or relationships too stationary, for GWR.

## When NOT to use

- Coefficients vary across space → use GWR / MGWR.
- No significant residual autocorrelation → plain OLS is fine.
- Very small `n` (< ~50) — ML estimation becomes unstable.

## Choosing Lag vs Error — LM tests

Run OLS first, then Lagrange Multiplier (LM) tests on residuals:

| LM-Lag sig? | LM-Error sig? | Choose |
|---|---|---|
| Yes | No  | Spatial **Lag** |
| No  | Yes | Spatial **Error** |
| Both sig | — | Compare **robust** LM-Lag vs robust LM-Error; pick the more significant |
| Neither | — | Stick with OLS |

## Critical constraints

1. **Build weights on the cleaned frame** — drop NAs, reset index, then `Queen.from_dataframe`.
2. **Row-standardize** — `w.transform = "r"`.
3. **`y` must be 2-D `(n, 1)`** — `gdf[[y_col]].values`, not `gdf[y_col].values`.
4. **No intercept column in `X`** — `spreg` adds it.
5. **Check residual Moran's I after fitting** — if still significant, model is under-specified.
6. **Report ρ (lag) or λ (error)** — these are *the* parameters that justify using the model.

## Paths

Use the three conventional variables from the step's INPUT / OUTPUT PATHS
section — **never hardcode filenames.**

- `INPUT_PATH` — input GeoPackage / CSV from Input Node Paths.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — primary GPKG/CSV with fitted + residuals.
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — directory for the coefficient CSV and any diagnostics.

## Canonical example (OLS → LM tests → SAR or SEM → residual check)

```python
import os
import geopandas as gpd
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
from libpysal.weights import Queen, KNN
from esda.moran import Moran
from spreg import OLS, ML_Lag, ML_Error

# INPUT_PATH / OUTPUT_NODE_PATH from the step's I/O section; OUTPUT_DIR pre-injected.
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

y_col  = "<DEPENDENT_VARIABLE>"
x_cols = ["<PREDICTOR_1>", "<PREDICTOR_2>", "<PREDICTOR_3>"]

# ---- 1. Clean & align ---------------------------------------------------
cols = [y_col] + x_cols
for c in cols:
    gdf[c] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[c], errors="coerce")
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=cols).reset_index(drop=True)

# ---- Guard against empty / tiny frames (usually caused by upstream join NaN) ----
if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows after dropping NA in {cols}. Check upstream join match rates.")
if len(gdf) < 10:
    print(f"[WARN] Only {len(gdf)} rows — spatial regression will be unreliable.")

y = gdf[[y_col]].values.astype(float)          # (n, 1)
X = gdf[x_cols].values.astype(float)           # (n, k), no intercept

# ---- 2. Weights ---------------------------------------------------------
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf)
if w.islands:
    w = KNN.from_dataframe(gdf, k=5)
w.transform = "r"

# ---- 3. OLS baseline with LM diagnostics --------------------------------
ols = OLS(y, X, w=w, spat_diag=True, moran=True, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
print(ols.summary)

lm_lag        = ols.lm_lag           # (stat, p)
lm_error      = ols.lm_error
rlm_lag       = ols.rlm_lag          # robust variants
rlm_error     = ols.rlm_error
print(f"LM-Lag   : stat={lm_lag[0]:.3f}, p={lm_lag[1]:.4f}")
print(f"LM-Error : stat={lm_error[0]:.3f}, p={lm_error[1]:.4f}")
print(f"Robust LM-Lag   : stat={rlm_lag[0]:.3f}, p={rlm_lag[1]:.4f}")
print(f"Robust LM-Error : stat={rlm_error[0]:.3f}, p={rlm_error[1]:.4f}")

# ---- 4. Pick model by LM rule ------------------------------------------
def pick_model(lm_lag, lm_error, rlm_lag, rlm_error, alpha=0.05):
    lag_sig, err_sig = lm_lag[1] < alpha, lm_error[1] < alpha
    if lag_sig and not err_sig: return "lag"
    if err_sig and not lag_sig: return "error"
    if lag_sig and err_sig:
        return "lag" if rlm_lag[1] < rlm_error[1] else "error"
    return "ols"

choice = pick_model(lm_lag, lm_error, rlm_lag, rlm_error)
print(f"LM decision: {choice.upper()}")

# ---- 5. Fit the chosen model -------------------------------------------
if choice == "lag":
    model = ML_Lag(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
    spatial_param = ("rho (ρ)", float(model.rho))
elif choice == "error":
    model = ML_Error(y, X, w=w, name_y=y_col, name_x=x_cols)
    spatial_param = ("lambda (λ)", float(model.lam))
else:
    model = ols
    spatial_param = ("n/a", np.nan)

print(model.summary)
print(f"Spatial parameter {spatial_param[0]} = {spatial_param[1]:.4f}")

# ---- 6. Residual Moran's I (did the model absorb the autocorrelation?) -
resid = np.asarray(model.u).flatten()
mi_resid = Moran(resid, w, permutations=999)
print(f"Residual Moran's I = {mi_resid.I:.4f}, p = {mi_resid.p_sim:.4f}")

# ---- 7. Save fitted values, residuals, coefficients --------------------
out = gdf.copy()
out["fitted"]   = np.asarray(model.predy).flatten()
out["residual"] = resid
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
out.to_file(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, driver="GPKG")

coef_df = pd.DataFrame({
    "variable": ["CONSTANT"] + x_cols,
    "beta":     np.asarray(model.betas).flatten()[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "std_err":  np.asarray(model.std_err).flatten()[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "z":        np.asarray([t[0] for t in model.z_stat])[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
    "p":        np.asarray([t[1] for t in model.z_stat])[: 1 + len(x_cols)],
})
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
coef_df.to_csv(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "spatial_regression_coefficients.csv"), index=False)

Key result attributes

Model Attribute Meaning
OLS ols.lm_lag, ols.lm_error (statistic, p-value) of LM tests
OLS ols.rlm_lag, ols.rlm_error Robust LM variants
SAR model.rho Spatial autoregressive parameter ρ
SEM model.lam Spatial error parameter λ
both model.betas, model.std_err, model.z_stat Coefficients, SE, (z, p)
both model.predy, model.u Fitted values, residuals
both model.pr2, model.aic, model.schwarz Pseudo-R², AIC, BIC

Interpretation

  • ρ > 0 (SAR): high y at a location raises y at its neighbors — positive spillover.
  • λ > 0 (SEM): unobserved shocks are spatially correlated; coefficients are still unbiased, but OLS SEs were wrong.
  • Coefficients in SAR are not marginal effects. Use spreg.diagnostics_sp or compute direct / indirect / total impacts for full interpretation.
  • After fitting, residual Moran's I should be non-significant. If it isn't, try MGWR, a mixed SAR-SEM (SARAR), or revisit predictors.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
Added intercept column to X spreg adds it — don't prepend ones.
y is 1-D gdf[[col]].values, not gdf[col].values.
Weights built on raw gdf before dropna Drop NAs, reset index, then build weights.
Interpreting SAR β as OLS β In SAR, effects propagate through W; compute impacts for marginal effects.
Using LM results without checking robust LM when both are significant Always fall back to the robust LM pair when the standard pair is jointly significant.
Residual Moran's I still significant Model under-specified — consider SARAR, GWR, or additional spatial predictors. 
```python
import os
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd

from libpysal.weights import Queen
from spreg import ML_Lag

# -----------------------------
# Paths (as provided)
# -----------------------------
COUNTIES_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_urbanrural_interaction_2019.gpkg"
WEIGHTS_GPKG_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/ca_county_queen_weights_2019.gpkg"

OUTPUT_NODE_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/spatial_lag_pm25_gini_metro_interaction_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787"

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# -----------------------------
# Load data
# -----------------------------
counties = gpd.read_file(COUNTIES_PATH)
w_gdf = gpd.read_file(WEIGHTS_GPKG_PATH)

# -----------------------------
# Validate / standardize geometry
# -----------------------------
counties = counties[counties.geometry.is_valid & ~counties.geometry.is_empty].copy()
w_gdf = w_gdf[w_gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~w_gdf.geometry.is_empty].copy()

# Align CRS to weights layer CRS (primary for contiguity)
if counties.crs != w_gdf.crs:
    counties = counties.to_crs(w_gdf.crs)

# -----------------------------
# Required columns (confirmed by inspection)
# -----------------------------
y_col = "pm25_mean_2019"
x_cols = ["B19083_001E:Gini Index", "Metro2013", "gini_x_metro"]
key_col = "GEOID"

# Ensure join key dtype consistency
counties[key_col] = counties[key_col].astype(str)
w_gdf[key_col] = w_gdf[key_col].astype(str)

# Join predictors onto the weights geometry frame to ensure weights keyed by GEOID
keep_cols = [key_col, y_col] + x_cols
counties_sub = counties[keep_cols].copy()
gdf = w_gdf[[key_col, "geometry"]].merge(counties_sub, on=key_col, how="inner")

# Coerce numeric fields (Metro2013 is int64 but keep robust coercion)
for c in [y_col] + x_cols:
    gdf[c] = pd.to_numeric(gdf[c], errors="coerce")

# Drop rows with missing model inputs
gdf = gdf.dropna(subset=[y_col] + x_cols).reset_index(drop=True)

if len(gdf) == 0:
    raise ValueError(f"No rows available after dropping NA in {[y_col] + x_cols}.")
if len(gdf) < 10:
    print(f"[WARN] Only {len(gdf)} observations after cleaning; ML SAR estimates may be unstable.")

# -----------------------------
# Build Queen contiguity weights keyed by GEOID
# -----------------------------
ids = gdf[key_col].tolist()
w = Queen.from_dataframe(gdf, ids=ids)

if getattr(w, "islands", None):
    if len(w.islands) > 0:
        raise ValueError(
            f"Queen weights contain islands (no neighbors) for GEOID(s): {w.islands}. "
            "Spatial lag (ML_Lag) may be invalid/unstable with islands; revise geography/weights."
        )

w.transform = "r"  # row-standardize

# -----------------------------
# Fit maximum-likelihood SAR (spatial lag) model
# -----------------------------
y = gdf[[y_col]].to_numpy(dtype=float)        # (n, 1)
X = gdf[x_cols].to_numpy(dtype=float)         # (n, k) -- no intercept; spreg adds constant

model = ML_Lag(
    y=y,
    x=X,
    w=w,
    name_y=y_col,
    name_x=x_cols,
    name_w="Queen(GEOID)"
)

# -----------------------------
# Build coefficient table
# -----------------------------
# betas includes: [CONSTANT, x1, x2, x3, rho]
betas = np.asarray(model.betas).flatten()
std_err = np.asarray(model.std_err).flatten()

# z_stat entries correspond to betas (including rho)
z_vals = np.array([zp[0] for zp in model.z_stat], dtype=float)
p_vals = np.array([zp[1] for zp in model.z_stat], dtype=float)

var_names = ["CONSTANT"] + x_cols + ["rho"]
coef_df = pd.DataFrame(
    {
        "variable": var_names,
        "coef": betas[: len(var_names)],
        "std_err": std_err[: len(var_names)],
        "z": z_vals[: len(var_names)],
        "p_value": p_vals[: len(var_names)],
    }
)

# Add model fit stats as repeated columns for easy manuscript use
fit_stats = {
    "n": int(model.n),
    "k": int(model.k),
    "aic": float(getattr(model, "aic", np.nan)),
    "bic": float(getattr(model, "schwarz", np.nan)),
    "pseudo_r2": float(getattr(model, "pr2", np.nan)),
}
for k, v in fit_stats.items():
    coef_df[k] = v

# -----------------------------
# Save primary output
# -----------------------------
coef_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

# Also save a manuscript-ready copy into tables/ and record it
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "spatial_lag_pm25_gini_metro_interaction_2019.csv")
coef_df.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="Maximum-likelihood spatial lag (SAR) model coefficients for county PM2.5 (2019) with Gini, Metro2013, and their interaction using Queen contiguity weights keyed by GEOID.",
    role="final",
    columns=list(coef_df.columns),
)

# Bivariate Correlation

## Description

Strength and direction of the association between **two** variables. Pearson for linear, Spearman/Kendall for monotonic/ordinal, point-biserial for continuous-vs-binary.

## When to use

- Testing one hypothesized pair of variables.
- Ranking a handful of predictors against a target.
- Correlating variables from two datasets after a key-based merge.

## When NOT to use

- Many pairwise pairs at once → use the Correlation Matrix skill.
- Spatial clustering of a single variable → use Moran's I.
- Non-monotonic relationships — correlation won't capture them.

## Choosing the method

| Method | Use when | Function |
|---|---|---|
| Pearson `r` | Both continuous and roughly linear | `scipy.stats.pearsonr` |
| Spearman `ρ` | Monotonic but non-linear, ordinal, or outlier-heavy | `scipy.stats.spearmanr` |
| Kendall `τ` | Small `n`, many ties | `scipy.stats.kendalltau` |
| Point-biserial | One variable is binary (0/1) | `scipy.stats.pointbiserialr` |

## Critical constraints

1. **Cast to numeric first** — `pd.to_numeric(col, errors="coerce")`.
2. **Drop NAs pairwise** — both columns must be non-null on the same rows.
3. **Always report `n`** alongside `r` and `p`.
4. **Zero-pad FIPS/ID keys as strings** before merging across datasets.

## Paths

- `INPUT_PATH` — from Input Node Paths. For cross-dataset merges, the step
  typically lists multiple inputs — read each by its listed path.
- `OUTPUT_NODE_PATH` — primary CSV with correlation statistics.
- `OUTPUT_DIR` — for the scatter PNG.

Never hardcode `"data.csv"`, `"dataset_a.csv"`, etc.

## Canonical example (Pearson + Spearman + Kendall + scatter)

```python
import os
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
import matplotlib
matplotlib.use("Agg")
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from scipy.stats import pearsonr, spearmanr, kendalltau

df = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH)

x_col = "<X_COLUMN>"
y_col = "<Y_COLUMN>"

# ---- 1. Cast + align -----------------------------------------------------
x = pd.to_numeric(df[x_col], errors="coerce")
y = pd.to_numeric(df[y_col], errors="coerce")
mask = x.notna() & y.notna()
x, y = x[mask], y[mask]
n = len(x)

# ---- 2. Three coefficients -----------------------------------------------
pr, pp = pearsonr(x, y)
sr, sp = spearmanr(x, y)
kr, kp = kendalltau(x, y)

results = pd.DataFrame([{
    "x": x_col, "y": y_col, "n": n,
    "pearson_r": round(pr, 4),  "pearson_p": round(pp, 6),
    "spearman_r": round(sr, 4), "spearman_p": round(sp, 6),
    "kendall_tau": round(kr, 4), "kendall_p": round(kp, 6),
}])
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
results.to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)
print(results.to_string(index=False))

# ---- 3. Scatter with trend line ------------------------------------------
fig, ax = plt.subplots(figsize=(8, 5))
ax.scatter(x, y, alpha=0.4, s=10, edgecolors="none")
z = np.polyfit(x, y, 1)
xs = np.linspace(x.min(), x.max(), 100)
ax.plot(xs, np.poly1d(z)(xs), "r--", linewidth=1.5)
ax.set_xlabel(x_col); ax.set_ylabel(y_col)
ax.set_title(f"{x_col} vs {y_col}  (Pearson r = {pr:.3f}, n = {n})")
fig.tight_layout()
os.makedirs(OUTPUT_DIR, exist_ok=True)
fig.savefig(os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "bivariate_scatter.png"), dpi=150)
plt.close(fig)

Cross-dataset variant (merge, then correlate)

import pandas as pd
from scipy.stats import pearsonr

# When the step has two inputs, they'll be listed separately in Input Node Paths.
df_a = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_A)
df_b = pd.read_csv(INPUT_PATH_B)

key_a, key_b = "<KEY_A>", "<KEY_B>"
var_a = "<VAR_FROM_A>"
vars_b = ["<VAR_FROM_B_1>", "<VAR_FROM_B_2>"]

df_a[key_a] = df_a[key_a].astype(str).str.strip()   # .str.zfill(5) for FIPS
df_b[key_b] = df_b[key_b].astype(str).str.strip()
df_a[var_a] = pd.to_numeric(df_a[var_a], errors="coerce")
for v in vars_b:
    df_b[v] = pd.to_numeric(df_b[v], errors="coerce")

merged = df_a.merge(df_b, left_on=key_a, right_on=key_b).dropna(subset=[var_a] + vars_b)

rows = []
for v in vars_b:
    r, p = pearsonr(merged[var_a], merged[v])
    rows.append({"pair": f"{var_a} vs {v}", "r": round(r, 4), "p": round(p, 6), "n": len(merged)})
import os
os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH), exist_ok=True)
pd.DataFrame(rows).to_csv(OUTPUT_NODE_PATH, index=False)

Interpretation

|r| range Strength
0.00 – 0.19 Very weak
0.20 – 0.39 Weak
0.40 – 0.59 Moderate
0.60 – 0.79 Strong
0.80 – 1.00 Very strong

Always report r, p, and n. Correlation is association, not causation.

Common pitfalls

Pitfall Fix
pearsonr fails on NaNs Drop pairwise: mask = x.notna() & y.notna().
Non-numeric dtype pd.to_numeric(col, errors="coerce").
Pearson on skewed / non-linear data Plot first; use Spearman/Kendall.
FIPS-code merge returns empty Cast both keys to string, zfill(5) county, zfill(2) state.
Many pairs without correction Apply Bonferroni/FDR when testing many hypotheses. 
```python
import os
import pandas as pd
import geopandas as gpd
from scipy.stats import spearmanr

INPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/counties_pm25_gini_urbanrural_2019.gpkg"
OUTPUT_PATH = "/bigdata/s0/tea5209/AGM/Outputs/a4c5a1b9-449e-440c-a2cf-003513b58787/pm25_gini_spearman_by_metro_2019.csv"
OUTPUT_DIR = os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH)

os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(OUTPUT_PATH), exist_ok=True)

# ---- Load -----------------------------------------------------------------
gdf = gpd.read_file(INPUT_PATH)

# Validate geometry (rule), though not used in correlation
if "geometry" in gdf.columns:
    gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.notna()]
    gdf = gdf[gdf.geometry.is_valid & ~gdf.geometry.is_empty]

x_col = "pm25_mean_2019"
y_col = "B19083_001E:Gini Index"
group_col = "Metro2013"

needed = [x_col, y_col, group_col]
missing = [c for c in needed if c not in gdf.columns]
if missing:
    raise KeyError(f"Missing columns: {missing}. Available columns: {list(gdf.columns)}")

# ---- Prep: cast to numeric, pairwise drop NAs -----------------------------
df = gdf[[group_col, x_col, y_col]].copy()
df[group_col] = pd.to_numeric(df[group_col], errors="coerce")
df[x_col] = pd.to_numeric(df[x_col], errors="coerce")
df[y_col] = pd.to_numeric(df[y_col], errors="coerce")

rows = []
for metro_val, label in [(1, "metro"), (0, "nonmetro")]:
    sub = df[df[group_col] == metro_val].copy()
    sub = sub.dropna(subset=[x_col, y_col])
    n = len(sub)

    if n < 2:
        rho, pval = float("nan"), float("nan")
    else:
        rho, pval = spearmanr(sub[x_col], sub[y_col])

    rows.append(
        {
            "group": label,
            "Metro2013": int(metro_val),
            "n": int(n),
            "x": x_col,
            "y": y_col,
            "spearman_rho": float(rho) if pd.notna(rho) else float("nan"),
            "spearman_p": float(pval) if pd.notna(pval) else float("nan"),
        }
    )

out_df = pd.DataFrame(rows)
out_df.to_csv(OUTPUT_PATH, index=False)

# Manuscript artifact (table)
tables_dir = os.path.join(OUTPUT_DIR, "tables")
os.makedirs(tables_dir, exist_ok=True)
table_path = os.path.join(tables_dir, "pm25_gini_spearman_by_metro_2019.csv")
out_df.to_csv(table_path, index=False)

record_table(
    output_dir=OUTPUT_DIR,
    file_path=table_path,
    caption="Spearman rank correlation between 2019 county PM2.5 and Gini Index, stratified by Metro2013 status, with sample sizes.",
    role="final",
    columns=["group", "Metro2013", "n", "spearman_rho", "spearman_p", "x", "y"],
)
